ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 30-1. - Authority of fire department to make bylaws. 
    The fire department is hereby empowered to make bylaws to promote its objects consistent with the laws of the state and ordinances of the town. 
(Code 1968, § 8-1)
State Law reference- Bylaws of fire department, Code of Virginia, § 27-7. 
Sec. 30-2. - Authorization for certain persons. 
    Pursuant to Section 40.1-79.1 of the Code of Virginia of 1950 as amended, the town hereby authorizes any person 16 years of age or older, with parental or guardian approval, to work with or participate fully in all activities of a volunteer fire company, provided such person has attained certification under National Fire Protection Association 1001, level one, fire fighter standards, as administered by the department of fire programs. 
(Ord. of 5-4-2004)
Secs. 30-3-30-25. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - FIRE PREVENTION 

Sec. 30-26. - Statewide Fire Prevention Code Act-Adopted. 
    In accordance with Code of Virginia, title 27, chapter 9 (§ 27-94 et seq.), the council hereby adopts the Virginia Statewide Fire Prevention Code Act, as amended (Code of Virginia, title 27, chapter 9, § 27-94 et seq.). 
(Code 1968, § 8-2.1)
Sec. 30-27. - Same-Administration, enforcement. 
    The act adopted in section 30-26 shall be administered and enforced by the fire marshal of the county; provided, that the fire marshal of the county shall notify the chief of police and the town manager before administering or enforcing such code in any particular incident. The fire marshal of the county shall have the authority to enforce the Virginia Statewide Fire Prevention Code Act (Code of Virginia, title 27, chapter 9, § 27-94 et seq.) upon a written complaint and/or upon discovery of a possible code violation. 
(Code 1968, § 8-2.2)
Sec. 30-28. - Blasting permit. 
    No person shall blast or carry on any blasting operations without having first secured therefor a permit from the town manager and a permit from the fire marshal of the county. Blasting or blasting operations conducted pursuant to such permits shall be carried on subject to such conditions as may be expressed in the permits. 
(Code 1968, § 8-9)
Charter reference- Adoption of Code of Virginia, § 15.1-865, pertaining to local powers as to explosive substances, § 4. 
Cross reference- Buildings and building regulations, ch. 14. 
Sec. 30-29. - Sale of firecrackers, etc., to minors prohibited. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to sell or offer for sale to any person under 18 years of age any firecracker, torpedo, skyrocket or other substance or thing of whatever form or construction containing nitrates, chlorates, oxalates, sulphides of lead, barium, antimony, nitroglycerin, phosphorus or any other explosive or inflammable compound or substance and intended, or commonly known, as fireworks. 
(Code 1968, § 8-1.1)
Cross reference- Offenses and miscellaneous provisions, ch. 46. 
State Law reference- Fireworks, Code of Virginia, § 59.1-142 et seq. 
Sec. 30-30. - Parking within fire lanes and fire apparatus access roads. 
    No person shall obstruct in any manner, including the parking of vehicles in any area designated as a fire lane or fire apparatus access road, as defined in the Virginia Statewide Fire Prevention Code. 
Exceptions: 
(1)	Buses, loading or unloading passengers, provided that the driver remains with the vehicle and able to move the vehicle if necessary. 
(2)	Fire, rescue, or law enforcement vehicles while they are involved in emergency operations.
(Ord. of 8-4-2009)
Sec. 30-31. - Obstructing fire hydrants. 
    Post, fences, vehicles, growth, trash, storage and other materials or objects shall not be placed or kept near fire hydrants, fire department inlet connections or fire protection system control valves in a manner that would prevent such equipment or fire hydrant from being immediately discernible. The fire department shall not be deterred or hindered from gaining immediate access to fire protection equipment or fire hydrant. 
(Ord. of 8-4-2009)
Sec. 30-32. - Penalties for violations of sections 30-30 and 30-31. 
    Any person violating any provision of sections 30-30 or 30-31 may be subject to fines as follows: 
(1)	Twenty dollars if paid within 30 calendar days at the town office.
(2)	If not paid within 30 calendar days, a summons may be issued, upon which a fine of not more than $250.00 may be assessed. 
    In addition to the above penalties, any vehicle parked in violation of section 30-30 or section 30-31 may be removed to a storage area in accordance with Code of Virginia, § 46.2-1213, provided, however, that no vehicle shall be removed from private property without the written request of the owner, or occupant of the premises. Any such removal shall be carried out by or under the direction of a law enforcement officer. As promptly as possible, each removal shall be reported to the county fire marshal and to the owner of the vehicle. Before regaining possession of the vehicle, the owner shall pay to the town all costs incidental to its removal and storage and locating the owner. Nothing in this section shall prevent any authorized officer from removing a vehicle in any emergency situation in such manner as he deems necessary. 
(Ord. of 8-4-2009)
Secs. 30-33-30-40. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - OPEN BURNING 

Sec. 30-41. - Title. 
    This article shall be known as the "Town of Woodstock Ordinance for the Regulation of Open Burning." 
(Ord. of 6-3-97(1))
Sec. 30-42. - Purpose. 
    The purpose of this article is to protect public health, safety, and welfare by regulating open burning within the town to achieve and maintain, to the greatest extend practicable, a level of air quality that will provide comfort and convenience while promoting economic and social development. This article is intended to supplement the applicable regulations promulgated by the state air pollution control board and other applicable regulations and laws. 
(Ord. of 6-3-97(1))
Sec. 30-42.1. - Enforcement and administration; permit required. 
    Open burning is prohibited unless a permit is obtained from the town manager and fire marshal. 
(Ord. of 3-4-2014(3))
Sec. 30-43. - Reserved. 
Editor's note- Ord. of March 4, 2014(3), repealed § 30-43, entitled "Definitions" which derived from Ord. of 6-3-97(1). 
Sec. 30-44. - Reserved. 
Editor's note- Ord. of March 4, 2014(3), repealed § 30-44, entitled "Prohibitions on open burning" which derived from Ord. of 6-3-97(1). 
Sec. 30-45. - Exemptions. 
    The following activities are exempted to the extent covered by the state air pollution control board's regulations for the control and abatement of air pollution: 
(1)	Open burning for training and instruction of government and public firefighters under the supervision of the designated official and industrial in-house firefighting personnel; 
(2)	Open burning for camp fires or other fires that are used solely for recreational purposes, for ceremonial occasions, for outdoor noncommercial preparation of food, and for warming of outdoor workers; 
(3)	Open burning for the destruction of any combustible liquid or gaseous material by burning in a flare or flare stack; 
(4)	Open burning for forest management and agriculture practices approved by the state air pollution control board; and 
(5)	Open burning for the destruction of classified military documents.
(Ord. of 6-3-97(1))
Sec. 30-46. - Reserved. 
Editor's note- Ord. of March 4, 2014(3), repealed § 30-46, entitled "Permissible open burning" which derived from Ord. of 6-3-97(1). 
Sec. 30-47. - Reserved. 
Editor's note- Ord. of March 4, 2014(3), repealed § 30-47, entitled "Permits" which derived from Ord. of 6-3-97(1). 
Sec. 30-48. - Penalties for violation. 
(a)	Any violation of this article is punishable as a class I misdemeanor.
(b)	Each separate incident may be considered a new violation.
(Ord. of 6-3-97(1))
Chapter 34 - HEALTH AND SANITATION[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Animals, ch. 10; rabies control, § 10-61 et seq.; buildings and building regulations, ch. 14; businesses, ch. 18; licensing of sale of patent medicines, § 18-81; nuisances generally, § 26-86; fire prevention and protection, ch. 30; manufactured homes and trailers, ch. 42; offenses and miscellaneous provisions, ch. 46; solid waste, ch. 62; utilities, ch. 82.
State Law reference- Nuisance birds, Code of Virginia, § 3.1-1011 et seq.; local abatement of nuisances, Code of Virginia, §§ 15.1-14(5), 15.1-867; local health ordinances to be at least as stringent as state laws and regulations, Code of Virginia, § 32.1-34.

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 34-1-34-25. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - CONDITION OF PREMISES 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 34-26. - Drainage of stagnant water and filling of marshes. 
    If any stagnant water or marshy place is found on any premises in the town, the owner thereof shall drain such stagnant water or fill such marsh within 30 days from notification by the town manager. Upon failure of the recipient to comply with such notice, the town manager may have the requisite work done at the expense of the town, and the expense thereof shall be collected from the owner in the same manner in which taxes and levies are collected. It shall be unlawful for the recipient of any such notice from the town manager to fail, neglect or refuse to comply therewith. 
(Code 1968, § 19-10)
Charter reference- Adoption of Code of Virginia, § 15.1-867, pertaining to areas that may be covered by stagnant water, § 4. 
State Law reference- Removal of unhealthful substances, Code of Virginia, § 15.1-11. 
Sec. 34-27. - Condition of drain or running water. 
    If, upon any ground in the town there shall be found a drain or running water, the owner thereof or the abutting property owners shall keep the same clean, free and unobstructed from trash, filth, garbage or vegetation. 
(Code 1968, § 19-11)
Sec. 34-28. - Permitting offensive liquids to flow onto the premises of another or street. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to permit any discharge from water closets, septic tanks, cesspools, or sinks or slop from kitchen or any offensive liquid to flow onto the premises of another or into any street. 
(Code 1968, § 19-12)
Sec. 34-29. - Permitting offensive, etc., hog pens, privies, etc., on premises. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to permit any hog pen, privy, chicken house or other building, which is offensive to the neighborhood or dangerous to health on any premises in the town. 
(Code 1968, § 19-13)
Cross reference- Animals, ch. 10. 
Sec. 34-30. - Keeping inoperative vehicles on residential or commercial property; removal by owner or town; lien. 
(a)	It shall be unlawful for any person to keep, except one within a fully enclosed building or structure or otherwise shielded or screened from public view, on any property zoned for residential or commercial purposes any motor vehicle, trailer or semitrailer, as such are defined in Code of Virginia, § 46.2-100, which is inoperative. An "inoperative motor vehicle" shall mean any motor vehicle which is not in operating condition or which, for a period of 60 days or longer, has been partially or totally disassembled by the removal of tires and wheels, the engine or other essential parts required for operation of the vehicle, or on which there are displayed neither valid license plates nor a valid inspection decal. However, the provisions of this section shall not apply to a licensed business which, on June 26, 1970, was regularly engaged in business as an automobile dealer, salvage dealer or scrap processor. 
(b)	The owners of property zoned for residential or commercial purposes shall, at such times as the council may prescribe, remove therefrom any such inoperative motor vehicles, trailers or semitrailers that are not kept within a fully enclosed building or structure. 
(c)	The council, through its own agents or employees, may remove any such inoperative motor vehicle, trailer or semitrailer, whenever the owner of the premises, after reasonable notice, has failed to do so. If the town council, through its own agents or employees, so removes any such vehicle after having given reasonable notice, the town may dispose of such vehicle after giving additional notice to the owner of the vehicle. The cost of any such removal and disposal shall be chargeable to the owner of the vehicle or premises and may be collected by the town as taxes and levies are collected. 
(d)	Every cost authorized by this section with which the owner of the premises shall have been assessed shall constitute a lien against the property from which the vehicle was removed, the lien to continue until actual payment of such costs shall have been made to the town. 
(Code 1968, § 19-15.1; Ord. of 9-4-2001)
Cross reference- Definitions and rules of construction generally, § 1-2; traffic and vehicles, ch. 78. 
State Law reference- Authority for above section, Code of Virginia, § 15.1-11.1. 
Sec. 34-30.1. - Removal and disposition of certain unattended vehicles; sale; disposition of proceeds. 
(a)	Whenever any motor vehicle, trailer or semitrailer is found on the public streets or public grounds unattended by the owner or operator and constitutes a hazard to traffic, or is parked in such manner as to be in violation of law, or whenever any motor vehicle, trailer or semitrailer is left unattended for more than 48 hours upon any public property or privately owned property other than the property of the owner of such motor vehicle, trailer or semitrailer, within the town or is abandoned upon such public property or privately owned property, without the permission of the owners, lessee or occupant thereof; any such motor vehicle, trailer or semitrailer may be removed for safekeeping by or under the direction of a police officer to a storage garage or area, or whenever any such vehicle is immobilized on a public roadway by weather conditions or other emergency situation; provided, however, that no such vehicle shall be so removed from privately owned premises without the written request of the owner, lessee or occupant thereof. 
(b)	The person at whose request such motor vehicle, trailer or semitrailer is removed from privately owned property shall indemnify the town against any loss or expense incurred by reason of removal, storage or sale thereof. It shall be presumed that such motor vehicle, trailer or semitrailer, or part thereof, is abandoned if (1) it lacks either: (a) a current license plate, (b) a current county or town plate or sticker or (c) a valid state inspection certificate or sticker, and (2) it has been in a specific location for four days without being moved. Each removal shall be reported immediately to the chief of police, who shall give notice to the owner of the motor vehicle, trailer or semitrailer as promptly as possible. The owner, before obtaining possession of the motor vehicle, trailer or semitrailer, shall pay to the town all reasonable costs incidental to the removal, storage and locating the owner of the motor vehicle, trailer or semitrailer. Should the owner fail or refuse to pay the costs or should the identity or whereabouts of the owner be unknown and unascertainable after a diligent search has been made, and after notice to the owner at his last known address and to the holder of any lien of record in the office of the department of motor vehicles against the motor vehicle, trailer or semitrailer, or part thereof, the vehicle shall be treated as an abandoned vehicle under the provisions of Article 1 (§ 46.2-1200, et seq.) of the Code of Virginia of 1950, as amended. 
(Ord. of 6-1-93(1); Ord. of 9-4-2001)
Sec. 34-31. - Removal, repair, etc., of buildings and other structures. 
(a)	The owners of property in the town shall at such time or times as the town council of the Town of Woodstock may prescribe, remove, repair or secure any building, wall or any other structure which might endanger the public health or safety of other residents of the town. 
(b)	The town council of the town through its own agents or employees may remove, repair or secure any building, wall or any other structure which might endanger the public health or safety of other residents of the town, wherein the owner and lien holder of such property after reasonable notice and a reasonable time to do so, has failed to remove, repair or secure said building, wall or other structure. For purposes of this section, reasonable notice shall include a written notice (i) mailed by certified or registered mail, return receipt requested, sent to the last known address of the property owner and (ii) published in a newspaper having general circulation in the town in accordance with the applicable provisions of § 15.1-504 of the Code of Virginia of 1950, as amended. No action shall be taken by the town to remove, repair or secure any building, wall or other structure for at least 30 days following the later of the return of the receipt or newspaper publication. 
(c)	In the event the town council of the town, through its own agents or employees removes, repairs or secures any building, wall or any other structure after complying with the notice provisions of this section, the cost or expenses thereof shall be chargeable to and paid by the owners of such property and may be collected by the town as taxes and levies are collected. 
(d)	Every charge authorized by this section with which the owner of any such property shall have been assessed and which remains unpaid shall constitute a lien against such property ranking on a parity with liens for unpaid town taxes and enforceable in the same manner as provided in Articles 3 (§ 58.1-3940 et seq.) and 4 (§ 58.1-3965 et seq.) of Chapter 39 of Title 58.1 of the Code of Virginia of 1950, as amended. 
(Ord. of 7-2-96(1))
Secs. 34-32-34-40. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - WEEDS, DEBRIS, ETC.[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Charter reference- Adoption of Code of Virginia, § 15.1-867, pertaining to the removal of weeds from private and public property, § 4.
State Law reference- Code of Virginia, §§ 15.2-901, 15.2-1115

Sec. 34-41. - Where prohibited generally. 
(a)	The owners of property therein shall, at such time or times as the town may prescribe, remove therefrom any and all trash, garbage, refuse, litter and other substances which might endanger the health or safety of other residents of the town; or may, whenever the town deems it necessary, after seven days, have such trash, garbage, refuse, litter and other like substances which might endanger the health of other residents of the town, removed by its own agents or employees, in which event the cost or expenses thereof shall be chargeable to and paid by the owners of such property and may be collected by the town as taxes are collected. Trash, garbage, refuse, litter and other debris shall be disposed of in personally owned or privately owned receptacles that are provided for such use and for the use of the persons disposing of such matter or in authorized facilities provided for such purpose and in no other manner not authorized by law. 
(b)	It shall be unlawful for the owner of any land or lot within the town to permit grass, weeds, brush and other foreign growth standing more than ten inches in height to remain upon so much of the property as lies within 100 feet of any dwelling house or commercial building. 
(Code 1968, § 19-16; Ord. of 11-6-2007)
Sec. 34-42. - Traffic hazard or menace to public safety. 
    It shall be unlawful for the owner of any land or lot within the town to permit any weeds, tree, shrub, hedge, flower or growth of vegetation of any kind to remain upon such land or lot in such location, size and condition as to constitute an obstruction or hindrance to the safe movement of vehicular and pedestrian traffic upon the streets and alleys of the town or as to constitute a menace to public safety. 
(Code 1968, § 19-17; Ord. of 11-6-2007)
Cross reference- Traffic and vehicles, ch. 78. 
Sec. 34-43. - Inspection of site and notice to remove. 
    The town manager or agents of the town shall, upon own initiative or when requested to do so in writing, investigate any land or lot. If it has been determined that there is a violation of section 34-41(a), 34-41(b) or 34-42, the town manager or an agent of the town shall notify the owner of the land or lot upon which the violation exists to cut and/or remove the condition. Such notice shall be in writing and delivered or mailed by certified mail to the last known address of the owner. If, after seven days from the receipt of the certified mail, the condition remains, the owner shall be deemed to be in violation of this division. Whenever the town deems it necessary, after seven days from the time of notice, the town manager or the town's agents shall have such grass, weeds, foreign growth or debris cut and/or removed in which event the cost and expenses thereof shall be chargeable to and paid by the owner of such property and may be collected by the town by billing or as taxes are collected. Every charge authorized by this section with which the owner of any such property shall have been assessed and which remains unpaid shall constitute a lien against such property ranking on a parity with liens for unpaid local taxes. 
(Code 1968, § 19-18; Ord. of 11-6-2007)
Sec. 34-44. - Penalty for violation of division. 
    Any person violating any of the provisions of this division shall be subject to a civil penalty, not to exceed $50.00 for the first violation, or violations arising from the same set of operative facts. The civil penalty for subsequent violations not arising from the same set of operative facts within 12 months of the first violation shall not exceed $200.00. Each business day during which the same violation is found to have existed shall constitute a separate offense. In no event shall a series of specified violations arising from the same set of operative facts result in civil penalties that exceed a total of $3,000.00 in a 12-month period. 
(Code 1968, § 19-20; Ord. of 11-6-2007)

ARTICLE II. - POLICE DEPARTMENT[3] 
Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
State Law reference- Powers and duties of police force, Code of Virginia, § 15.1-138.

DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 38-26. - Composition. 
    The police department shall consist of a chief of police and such other officers and patrol officers as the council, upon recommendation of the town manager, may deem necessary for the protection of the lives and property of the citizens and the enforcement of state laws, town ordinances and resolutions. 
(Code 1968, § 17-1)
State Law reference- Organization of town police forces, Code of Virginia, § 15.1-131.7. 
Sec. 38-27. - Control by town manager. 
    The police department shall be under the control of the town manager for the purpose of preserving and enforcing peace and order, for the execution of the laws of the state and this Code and other ordinances of the town, and the performance of such other duties as the town manager may prescribe. 
(Code 1968, § 17-2)
Sec. 38-28. - Oath of office. 
    Every member of the police department, before entering upon the discharge of his duties as such, shall take the oath of office prescribed by the state. A certificate of such oath shall be filed with the town manager. 
(Code 1968, § 17-3)
State Law reference- Oath of town officers, Code of Virginia, §§ 15.1-38, 49-1. 
Sec. 38-29. - Filling vacancies. 
    Subject to section 38-51, the town manager may appoint police officers to fill such vacancies as may occur. He shall report such appointments to the council at its next regular meeting. All appointments under this section shall be made subject to Code of Virginia, §§ 9-179-9-181 and 15.1-131.8, as well as physical examination and examination as to knowledge of the laws, ordinances and regulations. The examination as to laws, ordinances and regulations shall be made by the town manager and may be either oral or written. The physical examination shall be made by such local physician as the town manager may designate. 
(Code 1968, § 17-4)
Sec. 38-30. - Emergency appointments. 
    In time of public emergency; at such times as there are insufficient numbers of regular police officers to preserve the peace, safety and good order of the town; or at any time for the purpose of training, the town manager may appoint as many special police officers as the public necessity may require; provided, that he shall report any such appointment and his reasons for so doing to the next regular meeting of the council. All appointments under this section shall be made subject to the third sentence of section 38-29. 
(Code 1968, § 17-5)
State Law reference- Organization, training and powers of auxiliary police forces, Code of Virginia, § 15.1-159.2; calling auxiliary police officers into service, uniforms, Code of Virginia, § 15.1-159.5. 
Sec. 38-31. - Uniforms. 
    All regular police officers, including the chief of police, shall wear what is known as a police officer's uniform, as prescribed by the town manager and furnished by the town. 
(Code 1968, § 17-6)
State Law reference- Unlawful wearing of officer's uniform or insignia, Code of Virginia, § 18.2-175. 
Sec. 38-32. - Powers of police officers and privates. 
    The officers and privates constituting the police force of the town are hereby invested with all the power and authority which formerly belonged to the office of constable at common law in taking cognizance of and in enforcing the criminal laws of the commonwealth and the ordinances and regulations of the town and all powers which, under the laws of the town, may enable them to discharge the duties of their office. 
(Code 1968, § 17-7)
State Law reference- Powers and duties of police force, Code of Virginia, § 15.1-138. 
Sec. 38-33. - Reserved. 
Editor's note- Ord. of May 6, 2014(1), repealed § 38-33 entitled "Duties of police officers generally" which derived from Code 1968, § 17-8. 
Sec. 38-34. - Reserved. 
Editor's note- Ord. of May 6, 2014(1), repealed § 38-34 entitled "Attendance; conformity to article; rules and regulations" which derived from Code 1968, § 17-9. 
Sec. 38-35. - Reserved.

DIVISION 2. - CHIEF OF POLICE[4] 

Footnotes: 
--- (4) --- 
Cross reference- Administration, ch. 2.
State Law reference- Police forces to include a chief of police, Code of Virginia, § 15.1-131.7; records kept by chief of police, Code of Virginia, § 15.1-135.1.

Sec. 38-51. - Appointment. 
    The council, in consultation with the town manager, shall appoint a chief of police, who shall be subject to the administrative control and supervision of the town manager. 
(Code 1968, § 17-15; Ord. of 5-6-2014(1))
Sec. 38-52. - Powers and duties generally. 
    The chief of police shall be the chief executive of the police department, but he shall always be subject to the orders and regulations of the town manager. He shall be under the control of the town manager, for the purpose of preserving and enforcing peace and order and executing the laws of the state and ordinances of the town. It shall be the duty of the police force to respect and obey orders of the chief not in conflict with the rules and regulations. It shall be his duty at all times, day or night, to preserve the public peace; prevent the commission of crimes, and arrest offenders; to protect the rights of persons and of property; to guard the public health; to report nuisances and obstructions in the streets, alleys and other public places; to provide proper police force at fires; to protect the firefighters and property at fires and to discharge such other duties as may be required of him by the town manager. When charges are filed in his office against any member of the police force, or when he shall be informed of any gross neglect of duty, he shall immediately transmit same to the town manager, together with the names of witnesses to be summoned, so that the charges may be fully investigated by the town manager. He shall be responsible for the good order of the town and for the general good conduct of the members of the police force. He shall pay frequent visits at uncertain times to various portions of the town, and thus be able to supervise the conduct of all subordinates. 
(Code 1968, § 17-16)
Cross reference- Fire prevention and protection, ch. 30; streets, sidewalks and other public places, ch. 66. 
Sec. 38-53. - Records and reports. 
    The chief of police shall make periodic reports in writing from time to time to the town manager as he may require, showing the condition of the police force, the number of times each police officer has been absent and the cause of such absence, the condition of the jail, the number of arrests and the causes of same and the number of ordinance violations reported. He shall keep a record compiled by himself of the work of each police officer, showing marks of credit in the performance of duty, and showing demerits and the cause therefor and any and all complaints with reference to any given member of the force. On the first day of each month, or as soon thereafter as practicable, he shall furnish the town manager with a consolidated written report of the activities of his department for the previous month. Forms for such reports shall be prepared and furnished by the town manager. The chief of police shall keep duplicate records in his office of the reports made to the town manager in pursuance of the requirements of this section. He shall keep records showing the name of each member of the police force, and the area in which each member is stationed from day to day, the date of appointment and time of removal or suspension, and the happening of any vacancies in the department. 
(Code 1968, § 17-17)
Sec. 38-54. - Furnishing town manager with certain information useful in town administration. 
    It shall be the duty of the chief of police to communicate to the town manager any information from the daily reports of members of the police department or other persons in regard to streets, lights and other matters which will be of use to the town manager in the administration of his office. 
(Code 1968, § 17-18)
Cross reference- Streets, sidewalks and other public places, ch. 66. 
Sec. 38-55. - Reserved. 
Editor's note- Ord. of May 6, 2014(1), repealed § 38-55 entitled "Absence from duty" which derived from Code 1968, § 17-19. 
Chapter 42 - MANUFACTURED HOMES AND TRAILERS[1] 
  

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Buildings and building regulations, ch. 14; businesses, ch. 18; grounds for revocation of license for trailer park or trailer camp, § 18-39; licensing of trailer parks, trailer camps, § 18-86; fire prevention and protection, ch. 30; health and sanitation, ch. 34; planning, ch. 54; streets, sidewalks and other public places, ch. 66; subdivisions, ch. 70; taxation, ch. 74; traffic and vehicles, ch. 78; utilities, ch. 82; zoning, ch. 90.
State Law reference- Regulation of location of mobile homes, Code of Virginia, § 15.1-466.1; campgrounds, Code of Virginia, § 35.1-1 et seq.; Virginia Industrialized Building Safety Law, Code of Virginia, § 36-70 et seq.; Virginia Manufactured Housing Construction and Safety Standards Law, Code of Virginia, § 36-85.2 et seq.; Manufactured Housing Licensing and Transaction Recovery Fund Law, Code of Virginia, § 36-85.16 et seq.; Mobile Home Lot Rental Act, Code of Virginia, § 55-248.41 et seq.

Sec. 42-1. - Parking of trailers. 
    It shall be unlawful within the town for any person to park or place, or allow to be parked or placed, any trailer, mobile home or similar type vehicle or dwelling on any street or other place in town, except in a trailer court; except, that one trailer may be parked or stored in an improved enclosed garage or accessory building, or on any lot or plot of land; provided, that no living quarters shall be maintained or any business practiced in such trailer while it is so parked or stored. Nothing in this section shall be construed so as to prevent or prohibit the trailer, mobile home or similar type vehicle or dwelling, being temporarily parked on a town street if permitted by the provisions of this Code and other ordinances of the town. 
(Code 1968, § 25-1)
Sec. 42-2. - Drainage and condition of plots of ground in trailer court. 
    All plots of ground in a trailer court shall be well-drained and kept in a clean and orderly manner by the owner or operator thereof. 
(Code 1968, § 25-2)
Sec. 42-3. - Requirements as to trailers and trailer camps located outside of town. 
(a)	Trailers on individual lots not in trailer parks or camps and trailer camps or parks located outside the town, but connected to the sewer and water systems, either or both, of the town shall comply with all applicable laws and regulations of the state board of health and shall have such area for parking spaces and such sanitary facilities and electrical connections as would meet the minimum standards set forth in chapter 90. Any trailer or trailer camp or park not meeting the requirements set forth in the foregoing provisions of this section shall be denied the use of the water and sewer facilities of the town. 
(b)	In addition to regular payments of water and sewerage charges, there shall be a quarterly service charge of $6.00 for each such trailer or trailer plot which is located outside the town and connected to the sewer and water systems, either or both, of the town. 
(c)	Nothing contained in this section shall prevent the discontinuance of sewer or water service, either or both, to any user outside the town when such discontinuance may be deemed in the best interest of the town by the town manager or the council. 
(Code 1968, § 25-3)
Cross reference- Buildings and building regulations, ch. 14; utilities, ch. 82. 
Sec. 42-4. - Effect of removal of wheels, etc. 
    Any action toward the removal of wheels or similar transporting devices from any trailer, except for temporary purposes of repair, or toward otherwise permanently attaching such trailer to the ground, shall subject such trailer to the requirements of all the provisions of this Code and other ordinances of the town relating to buildings and structures. 
(Code 1968, § 25-4)
Cross reference- Buildings and building regulations, ch. 14. 
Sec. 42-5. - Penalty for violation of chapter. 
    Any person violating any provision of this chapter shall, upon conviction, be fined not less than $50.00 nor more than $500.00 for each offense. 
(Code 1968, § 25-5)

Editor's note- Ord. of May 6, 2014(2), repealed § 46-3 entitled "Attempts to commit misdemeanors; how punished" and derived from Code 1968, § 14-5; Ord. of 7-2-91(12), § 14-5. 
Sec. 46-4. - Audible alarms. 
(a)	Definition. As used in this section, "audible alarm" means a device designed for the detection of unauthorized entry or fire on protected premises, which generates an audible sound when it is activated. 
(b)	Posting of notice. Every person maintaining or using an audible alarm shall post a current notice containing the names and telephone numbers of the persons to be notified for rendering repairs or service and securing the protected premises during any hour of the day or night when the audible alarm is activated. Such notice shall be posted near the alarm in a position so that it is legible from the ground level adjacent to the location of the audible alarm. Any violation of this section shall be a class 4 misdemeanor. 
(c)	Deactivation. Any audible alarm, once activated, must be silenced within 30 minutes, either manually or by an automatic cutoff device. Any violation of this subsection shall be a class 4 misdemeanor. 
(d)	Fees and penalties for false alarms. 
(1)	The owner or lessee of any alarm shall be penalized a fee of $50.00 for each false alarm in excess of four transmitted by such device in any 12-month period, which resulted in a response by police, fire, rescue or other emergency services personnel, and shall be penalized a fee of $100.00 for each such false alarm in excess of eight transmitted by such device in any 12-month period, which resulted in a response by police, fire, rescue or other emergency services personnel. 
(2)	The discretion as to which alarms are false shall be with the town manager and the chief of police. 
(3)	The chief of police shall administer the collection of fees and penalties imposed by this section and shall promptly transmit all such fees and penalties collected to the town treasurer. 
(4)	An alarm intentionally activated by a person in violation of section 46-5 or Code of Virginia, § 18.2-212, shall not be a false alarm for the purposes of this section. 
(Code 1968, § 14-29)
Cross reference- Definitions and rules of construction generally, § 1-2; fire prevention and protection, ch. 30; law enforcement, ch. 38. 
State Law reference- Local regulation of alarm company operators, Code of Virginia, § 15.1-28.2.

Sec. 46-12. - Dumping trash, etc., on public or private property. 
(a)	No person shall dump or otherwise dispose of ashes, dirt, trash, garbage, refuse, litter or other unsightly matter on public property, including a public highway, right-of-way or property adjacent to such highway or right-of-way, or on private property without the written consent of the owner thereof or his agent. 
(b)	When any person is arrested for a violation of this section, and the matter alleged to have been illegally dumped or disposed of has been ejected from a motor vehicle, the arresting officer may comply with the provisions of Code of Virginia, § 46.2-936, in making such arrest. 
(c)	When a violation of the provisions of this section has been observed by any person, and the matter illegally dumped or disposed of has been ejected from a motor vehicle, the owner or operator of such motor vehicle shall be presumed to be the person ejecting such matter. However, such presumption shall be rebuttable by competent evidence. 
(d)	Any person convicted of a violation of this section shall be guilty of a class 1 misdemeanor.
(e)	The provisions of this section shall not apply to the lawful disposal of such matter in landfills. 
(Code 1968, §§ 14-19, 14-31.1, 19-2, 21-8)
Cross reference- Solid waste, ch. 62. 
State Law reference- Containers for deposit of litter, Code of Virginia, § 10.1-1419 et seq.; allowing escape of load material, penalty, Code of Virginia, § 10.1-1424; throwing or depositing certain substances upon highway, Code of Virginia, § 18.2-324; dumping trash, etc., on highway, right-of-way or private property, Code of Virginia, § 33.1-346.

    It shall be unlawful for any person to conduct more than four yard sales within the town in any calendar year at any household, residence or business location, or otherwise. (Code 1968, § 14-28; Ord. of 1-4-2011)

Sec. 46-29. - Urinating on public property. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to urinate in or on any public street, sidewalk or any other public property or private property open to the public, except in toilets open to the public. Any person violating the provisions of this section shall be fined not more than $250.00. 
(Ord. of 4-3-2007)

ARTICLE IV. - WEAPONS[4] 

Footnotes:

Sec. 46-116. - Discharging firearms. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to discharge firearms within the town. This section shall not apply to military companies or military schools acting under permission of the town manager or to any licensed shooting gallery. For the purpose of this section, firearm shall mean any weapon in which ammunition may be used or discharged by explosion or pneumatic pressure. 
(Code 1968, § 28-1; Ord. of 5-6-2014(2))
State Law reference- Willfully discharging firearms in public places, Code of Virginia, § 18.2-280; shooting in or along road or in street, Code of Virginia, § 18.2-286.

(Code 1968, § 28-3)

(Ord. of 3-3-98(1))
Chapter 50 - PARKS AND RECREATION[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Editor's note-Pursuant to § 4 of the town charter, the following are applicable to the town: Code of Virginia, § 15.1-858 (swimming pools, lakes and other waters); Code of Virginia, § 15.1-871 (use of and damage to parks, recreational facilities, etc.); and Code of Virginia, § 15.1-874 (municipal parks, playfields, playgrounds, etc.).
Cross reference- Definitions and rules of construction generally, § 1-2; administration, ch. 2; animals, ch. 10; animals in parks, § 10-1; fire prevention and protection, ch. 30; planning, ch. 54; streets, sidewalks, and other public places, ch. 66; definitions relating to subdivisions, § 70-1; zoning, ch. 90; definitions relating to zoning, § 90-1; purposes of zoning chapter, § 90-2.
State Law reference- Town parks and playgrounds, Code of Virginia, § 15.1-15; systems of public recreation and playgrounds, Code of Virginia, § 15.1-271 et seq.; liability of town in the operation of recreational facilities, Code of Virginia, § 15.1-291.

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 50-1-50-35. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - PARK COMMISSION[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Cross reference- Administration, ch. 2.

Sec. 50-36. - Creation; composition; appointment, term, removal and compensation of members. 
    A park commission is hereby created for the town. Such commission shall consist of five members, one of whom shall be a member of the council and the remaining four shall be qualified voters of the town. The mayor shall appoint the members of the commission and shall make appointments to fill vacancies for the unexpired terms. The term of the councilmanic member shall in all cases correspond with his term of office. The other members shall be appointed for staggered terms of four years. Any appointed member may be removed from office by a two-thirds vote of the council. The compensation of the members of the commission shall be such as the council may from time to time direct. 
(Code 1968, § 18-1)
Sec. 50-37. - Power to act as advisory body and to make recommendations. 
    The park commission is authorized and empowered to act as an advisory body and make recommendations to the council and to the department of recreation for the development of parks and playgrounds and for the beautification of the streets and other public places within the town. 
(Code 1968, § 18-2)
Cross reference- Streets, sidewalks and other public places, ch. 66. 
Chapter 54 - PLANNING[1] 
Footnotes:

ARTICLE II. - PLANNING COMMISSION[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Cross reference- Administration, ch. 2; town manager to attend meetings of planning commission, § 2-205.

Sec. 54-36. - Creation. 
    Pursuant to state law, a planning commission for the town is hereby created. 
(Code 1968, § 15-1)
State Law reference- Creation of local planning commissions, Code of Virginia, § 15.1-427.1. 
Sec. 54-37. - Composition, appointment and term of members. 
    The planning commission shall be composed of six members, who shall be appointed by the council, all of whom shall be residents of the town, qualified by knowledge and experience to make decisions on questions of community growth and development. At least one-half of the members so appointed shall be owners of real property. One member of the commission may be a member of the council, and one member may be a member of the administrative branch of government of the town. The term of each of these two members shall be coextensive with the term of office to which he has been elected or appointed unless the council, at the first regular meeting each year, appoints others to serve as their representatives. The remaining members of the commission shall serve for terms of four years each. 
(Code 1968, § 15-2)
State Law reference- Similar provisions, Code of Virginia, § 15.1-437. 
Sec. 54-38. - Compensation. 
    In accordance with Code of Virginia, § 15.1-437, the council may by a majority vote provide for: 
(1)	Reimbursement of actual expenses incurred by members of the commission;
(2)	Compensation to such members, or any of them, for their services; or
(3)	Both.
(Code 1968, § 15-3)
Sec. 54-39. - Removal of members. 
    Any member of the planning commission may be removed from office for malfeasance in office. 
(Code 1968, § 15-4)
State Law reference- Similar provisions, Code of Virginia, § 15.1-437. 
Sec. 54-40. - Filling vacancies. 
    Vacancies upon the planning commission, however caused, shall be, to conform with state law, filled by the council for the unexpired term only. 
(Code 1968, § 15-5)
State Law reference- Similar provisions, Code of Virginia, § 15.1-437. 
Sec. 54-41. - Functions, powers, duties and limitations. 
    The planning commission shall have the functions, powers and duties, and be subject to the limitations which are prescribed by law. 
(Code 1968, § 15-6)
State Law reference- Duties of planning commissions, Code of Virginia, § 15.1-444. 
Chapter 58 - SECONDHAND GOODS[1] 
  

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Businesses, ch. 18; licensing of sale of junk, secondhand articles, etc., § 18-78 et seq.; licensing of pawnbrokers, § 18-82; zoning, ch. 90.
State Law reference- Ordinances taxing and regulating automobile graveyards and junkyards, Code of Virginia, § 15.1-28; regulation of secondhand dealers, pawnshops, etc., Code of Virginia, § 15.1-866; junkyards, Code of Virginia, § 33.1-348.

Sec. 58-1. - Establishment, maintenance, etc., of junkyards, etc., exposed to weather. 
(a)	Except as provided in this chapter, it shall be unlawful for any person to establish, conduct, operate or maintain, within the town, any junkyard or place of business, which is exposed to the weather, where the business of the buying, selling, collecting or storing of junk is carried on. 
(b)	The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this section, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Junkyard means an establishment or place of business which is maintained, operated, or used for storing, keeping, buying, or selling junk, or for the maintenance or operation of an automobile graveyard, and the term shall include garbage dumps and sanitary fills. 
(c)	This section shall not be operative upon and apply to any junkyard which was established and operating legally within the town prior to November 1, 1952, but the provisions in this subsection shall not be construed to permit any expansion or enlargement of any existing junkyard, nor shall it be construed to permit the sale, transfer or assignment of either ownership or operation of any existing junkyard, as referred to in subsection (a). 
(d)	Any violation of this code section shall be a Class 2 misdemeanor.
(Code 1968, § 19-14; Ord. of 7-1-2014(1))
Cross reference- Definitions and rules of construction generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 58-2. - Establishment, maintenance, etc., of automobile graveyards, etc. 
(a)	It shall be unlawful for any person to establish, conduct, operate or maintain within the town any automobile graveyard or wrecking yard where wrecked, obsolete or old automobiles, trucks, tractors and other vehicles are collected, junked, stored, dismantled or kept for sale, either assembled or unassembled. 
(b)	The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this section, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Automobile graveyard means any lot or place which is exposed to the weather and upon which more than five motor vehicles of any kind, incapable of being operated, and which it would not be economically practical to make operative, are placed, located or found. 
(c)	Any violation of this code section shall be a Class 2 misdemeanor.
(Code 1968, § 19-15; Ord. of 7-1-2014(1))
Cross reference- Definitions and rules of construction generally, § 1-2; traffic and vehicles, ch. 78. 
Chapter 60 - VENDORS (SOLICITORS) 
ARTICLE I. - DOOR-TO-DOOR SOLICITORS 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 60-1. - Definition. 
    For the purpose of this article, a solicitor is any person who goes from house to house or from place to place in the town, selling or taking orders for, or offering to sell or take orders for, goods, wares or merchandise, or any article for future delivery, or for services to be performed presently in the future or for the making, manufacturing or repairing of any article or thing for present or future delivery and who demands, accepts or receives payment or a deposit of money in advance of final delivery. A solicitor does not include, however, solicitors or hucksters of fresh farm products produced by such solicitors or hucksters, solicitors of newspapers or persons licensed by the Commonwealth of Virginia under Title 38.2 of the Code of Virginia, pertaining to the sale of insurance. 
(Ord. of 2-2-2010)
Sec. 60-2. - Form and contents of orders; copy to be given to purchaser. 
    All orders taken by solicitors shall be in writing, in duplicate, stating the terms thereof, the amount paid in advance, the name, address and telephone number of the solicitor's employer and one copy shall be given to the purchaser. 
(Ord. of 2-2-2010)
DIVISION 2. - PERMIT 

Sec. 60-3. - Required. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to act as a solicitor within the town without first having secured a permit from the police department to do so. 
(Ord. of 2-2-2010)
Sec. 60-4. - Application. 
    Any person desiring a permit required by this division, shall make application therefor to the police department on a form to be provided by that department, stating the name and address of the applicant, the name and address of the person, firm or corporation that he represents, and the kind of goods offered for sale, or the kind of services to be performed and any other information on the applicant deemed necessary by the police department for public safety. 
(Ord. of 2-2-2010)
Sec. 60-5. - Fee. 
    The person securing a solicitor's permit shall pay a fee of $20.00 therefor to the town treasurer. 
(Ord. of 2-2-2010)
Sec. 60-6. - Term. 
    A permit issued under this division, shall be in effect for a period of one year. 
(Ord. of 2-2-2010)
Sec. 60-7. - To be carried and produced for inspection. 
    Every permit issued under this division, shall be carried at all times by the holder of the permit and shall be produced for inspection upon demand of any police officer of the town or person being solicited. 
(Ord. of 2-2-2010)
Sec. 60-7.1. - Failure to obtain permit. 
    Any violation of article 1 shall be guilty of a Class 3 misdemeanor. 
(Ord. of 7-1-2014(2))
ARTICLE II. - COMMERCIAL SOLICITATIONS FOR CHARITABLE ORGANIZATIONS 

Sec. 60-8. - Exemptions from article. 
    This article shall not apply to the public solicitation of funds by the sale of tickets, tags, contributions, advertising or otherwise, for events, activities and enterprises described in section 60-9, by the regularly constituted and duly authorized members of bona fide nonprofit organizations, religious, charitable, fraternal, patriotic, political, civic, or philanthropic, where the entire funds or proceeds derived from such enterprise revert to and belong to such organization. 
(Ord. of 2-2-2010)
Sec. 60-9. - License required. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person representing or pretending to represent, directly or indirectly, or using the name of, any nonprofit, charitable, philanthropic, educational, patriotic, political or labor organization, lodge or club or any other like association or society, to solicit funds for a public dance, entertainment, charity advertising scheme or similar purposes, through the sale of tickets, tags, contributions, advertising or any other method, where such person shares or receives, directly or indirectly, any part of such fund for such solicitation and promotion, without having first procured a license to do so pursuant to the provisions of section 60-3, et seq. 
(Ord. of 2-2-2010)
Sec. 60-10. - Misrepresentations in application for license. 
    Any misrepresentation or misstatement of a required fact in an application for a license required by section 60-9 shall be sufficient ground for the withholding or revocation of the license and shall constitute a Class 3 misdemeanor. 
(Ord. of 2-2-2010)
Chapter 62 - SOLID WASTE[1] 
  
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Charter reference- Adoption of Code of Virginia, § 15.1-857, pertaining to garbage and refuse disposal, § 4.
Cross reference- Administration, ch. 2; health and sanitation, ch. 34; discarding or abandoning iceboxes, etc., § 46-9; dumping trash, etc., on public or private property, § 46-12; utilities, ch. 82; supplementary zoning regulations, § 90-376 et seq.; home occupations, § 90-377.
State Law reference- Virginia Waste Management Act, Code of Virginia, § 10.1-1400 et seq.; removal of trash, garbage, weeds, etc., from property, Code of Virginia, § 15.1-11; contracts for garbage and refuse pickup and disposal services, waste recovery facilities, Code of Virginia, § 15.1-28.02; ordinances requiring delivery of garbage, trash and refuse to certain facilities, Code of Virginia, § 15.1-28.03; regulation of garbage and refuse pickup and disposal services, Code of Virginia, § 15.1-28.1; mailing of summons for violation of trash ordinance, Code of Virginia, § 19.2-76.2; dumping trash, etc., on highway, right-of-way or private property, Code of Virginia, §§ 33.1-346, 33.1-346.1; dump creating fire hazard to public bridge, Code of Virginia, § 33.1-347.

ARTICLE I. - REFUSE COLLECTION 

Sec. 62-1. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Garbage includes kitchen and table refuse, offal and every accumulation of animal and vegetable matter which attend the preparation, dealing in, and storage of food, meats, fruits, vegetables and other provisions for human subsistence. 
    Trash includes paper, rags, paper containers, wooden boxes, tin cans, glass bottles and all household wastes and yard cuttings. 
(Code 1968, § 19-1)
Cross reference- Definitions and rules of construction generally, § 1-2. 
State Law reference- Definitions for the Virginia Waste Management Act, Code of Virginia, § 10.1-1400; definitions concerning litter control and recycling, Code of Virginia, § 10.1-1414; definitions concerning the siting of hazardous waste facilities, Code of Virginia, § 10.1-1433. 
Sec. 62-2. - Placing nuisances, etc., on premises, etc. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to place on the private premises of any person, whether his own or that of another, or to allow to remain on premises owned or occupied by him, any rubbish, wastepaper or anything dangerous, offensive or unhealthy, or to maintain or permit a nuisance of any kind on his premises. 
(Code 1968, § 19-2)
Cross reference- Nuisances, § 26-86 et seq. 
Sec. 62-3. - Placing or allowing trash where it constitutes a fire hazard. 
    Trash shall not be placed or allowed to remain where it will constitute a fire hazard. 
(Code 1968, § 19-3)
Cross reference- Fire prevention and protection, ch. 30. 
Sec. 62-4. - Garbage to be disposed of promptly or placed in containers; setting out containers for collection, etc., of garbage; removal of containers. 
(a)	All garbage shall be disposed of promptly or placed in containers to be provided by the householder. These containers shall be placed on the curb no earlier than 5:00 p.m. the day before regular weekly collection and no later than 7:00 a.m. the day of regular collection. 
(b)	The householder shall remove the nondisposable containers from public view before sundown on such collection days. 
(Code 1968, § 19-4; Ord. of 1-8-2002; Ord. of 6-7-2011)
Sec. 62-5. - Kind of containers; protection from animals. 
    All garbage and other offensive matter shall be kept in closed containers of five- to 50-gallon capacity with a tightfitting lid or plastic or plastic-type bag containers, securely tied, and placed secure from flies, rodents, dogs and other animals. For containers with greater than 50-gallon capacity, garbage will be placed within a plastic or plastic-type bag containers, may be more than one bag, securely tied, within the greater than 50-gallon capacity container. 
(Code 1968, §§ 19-4, 19-5; Ord. of 6-7-2011)
Cross reference- Animals, ch. 10. 
Sec. 62-6. - Liquids in garbage containers. 
    Liquids shall not be poured or placed in the containers for garbage. 
(Code 1968, § 19-6)
Sec. 62-7. - Containers, etc., for trash. 
    All trash shall be placed in a container per the provisions of section 62-5 of this chapter, or made into a bundle so that it may be readily moved and carried without coming apart or spilling. 
(Code 1968, § 19-7; Ord. of 6-7-2011)
Sec. 62-8. - Removal of garbage and trash by town. 
    Garbage and trash will be removed from premises in the town by the town, or its agent, when such garbage and trash is put into containers or made into bundles as provided in this chapter. The fee for garbage and trash removal from premises shall be set by the town council. 
(Code 1968, § 19-8; Ord. of 3-4-2008; Ord. of 6-7-2011)
Sec. 62-9. - Penalty for violation; evidence of violation. 
    Any person violating any of the provisions of this chapter shall be guilty of a class 4 misdemeanor. The presence of trash or garbage on the private premises of any person or adjacent thereto shall be prima facie evidence of a violation of this chapter. 
(Code 1968, § 19-9)
Secs. 62-10-62-19. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - CURBSIDE RECYCLING 

Sec. 62-20. - Purpose. 
    This council finds that reduction of the solid waste stream through recycling efforts is one effective means of addressing the growing problem and related escalating costs of solid waste disposal. Recycling should also aid in conservation of our nation's material resources. For these reasons, the council finds that the public interest will be better served if the following provisions are enacted to enable the town's curbside recycling program to operate as efficiently as is practicable. 
(Ord. of 6-7-2011)
Sec. 62-21. - Voluntary recycling program. 
    All curbside customers may participate in the town-wide residential recycling program by (1) collecting all of their recyclable materials, and (2) placing such materials in recycling containers in the same location and manner as refuse is placed on the designated day for collection of those materials. Recycling containers shall be removed in the same manner as refuse containers. 
(Ord. of 6-7-2011)
Sec. 62-22. - Ownership of recycling containers. 
    Title to all recycling containers provided to customers by the town or its agent shall remain with the town or its agent. In the event a customer moves, the customer shall leave the recycling container behind to be used by the next customer occupying the property being served. 
(Ord. of 6-7-2011)
Sec. 62-23. - Ownership of recyclable materials. 
    Once a customer places recyclable materials in a recycling container at a designated curbside collection point, title to those materials shall be deemed to be vested in the town or its designated agent. No person shall remove, take, collect or transport any recyclable material that has been placed in a recycling container from any curbside, street right-of-way, alley or other designated collection point without the express authority of the town. 
(Ord. of 6-7-2011)
Sec. 62-24. - Sole purpose of recycling containers. 
    No person shall use recycling containers for anything but participation in the town's curbside recycling program. No person may place garbage or other refuse in a recycling container. It shall be unlawful for any person to borrow, steal, damage or otherwise remove any recycling container from use in the curbside recycling program. 
(Ord. of 6-7-2011)
Sec. 62-25. - Additional recycling regulations. 
    The town is hereby authorized to publish, implement and enforce reasonable regulations necessary to administer the town's curbside recycling program. Such regulations shall serve as a supplement to this article. 
(Ord. of 6-7-2011)
Secs. 62-26-62-40. - Reserved. 
Chapter 66 - STREETS, SIDEWALKS, AND OTHER PUBLIC PLACES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Charter reference- Adoption of Code of Virginia, § 15.1-889, pertaining to streets, sidewalks and public ways generally; Code of Virginia, § 15.1-890, pertaining to streets, highways, etc., outside the municipal corporation; and Code of Virginia, § 15.1-893, pertaining to obstructions or encroachments, § 4.
Cross reference- Administration, ch. 2; buildings and building regulations, ch. 14; definitions relating to businesses, § 18-1; licensing of contracting occupations, etc., § 18-159; general powers and duties of chief of police, § 38-52; chief of police to furnish certain information to town manager, § 38-54; manufactured homes and trailers, ch. 42; parks and recreation, ch. 50; powers of park commission, § 50-37; planning, ch. 54; subdivisions, ch. 70; streets in subdivisions, § 70-112; curbs and sidewalks in subdivisions, § 70-124 et seq.; taxation, ch. 74; traffic and vehicles, ch. 78; permits for parades and processions, § 78-12; utilities, ch. 82; vehicles for hire, ch. 86; site plans, § 90-391.
State Law reference- Authority of town to lay off streets, walks or alleys; alter, improve and light the same; and to permit the temporary use of streets for other than public purposes, Code of Virginia, § 15.1-14(1), (9); limited access streets, Code of Virginia, § 15.1-16; assessments for local improvements, Code of Virginia, § 15.1-239 et seq.; municipal streets and alleys generally, Code of Virginia, §§ 15.1-363 et seq., 15.1-888 et seq.; franchises, Code of Virginia, § 15.1-894; state highway plat book, Code of Virginia, § 17-69.1; state highway system, Code of Virginia, § 33.1-25 et seq.; occupation of streets, etc., without consent of corporate authorities, Code of Virginia, § 56-14; pipelines and other works in streets and alleys, Code of Virginia, § 56-257 et seq.

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 66-1. - Plan and survey of town. 
    The survey and plan of the town, showing distinctly each lot, public street and alley therein, the size and number of lots and the width of the streets and alleys, with such explanations and remarks as deemed proper, caused to be made by the street committee of the council, pursuant to ordinance of February 9, 1921, approved by the council, entered in the record book of the council and recorded in the clerk's office of the county, shall remain in such office and be prima facie evidence of the boundaries of such lots, streets and alleys of the town. 
(Code 1968, § 21-1)
Sec. 66-2. - Reserved. 
Editor's note- Ord. of July 1, 2014(3), repealed § 66-2 entitled "Signs, banners, etc." and derived from Code 1968, § 21-2. 
Sec. 66-3. - Removal of snow. 
    It shall be unlawful for the occupant of any building, and, where there is no occupant for the owner of such vacant lot or building or any unimproved lot of land, lying on the street, alley or public walk, within the town, where there is a paved footway or sidewalk, to permit snow to remain along the front or side of such premises longer than two hours after the same has ceased to fall, except that if the snow shall cease to fall in the nighttime, it shall be cleared away by 12:00 p.m. the following afternoon. Each violation of this section shall be punished as provided by section 1-7, and if the occupant or owner of the premises, as the case may be, fails or refuses to clean off the snow in accordance herewith, it shall be the duty of the town manager to cause such pavement or sidewalk to be cleaned at the cost of such occupant or owner. 
(Code 1968, § 21-3; Ord. of 11-6-2007; Ord. of 7-1-2014(3))
Charter reference- Adoption of Code of Virginia, § 15.1-867, pertaining to municipal powers as to removal of snow from sidewalks, § 4. 
Cross reference- Law enforcement, ch. 38. 
State Law reference- Code of Virginia, § 15.2-1115. 
Sec. 66-4. - Porches, cellar doors, etc., constructed or erected in or upon sidewalk. 
(a)	It shall be unlawful for any person to construct or erect any platform, porch, stairway, cellar door, cellarway or awning post in or upon any sidewalk or pavement. When any sidewalk or pavement having such obstruction is rebuilt, the same shall be removed. 
(b)	At those places where awning posts or cellar doors are on February 9, 1921, in any sidewalk or pavement, the same shall be permitted to remain upon condition that such awning posts be constructed of metal, designed to fit into the curb and be secured by bolts fitted into holes and leaded, and such cellar doors shall run lengthwise with the walk, extending into the same not exceeding 21/2 feet and opening towards the street, and shall remain erect when open and the hinges shall be flush with the surface of such sidewalk or pavement. 
(Code 1968, § 21-4; Ord. of 7-1-2014(3))
Cross reference- Buildings and building regulations, ch. 14. 
Secs. 66-5-66-35. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - PROHIBITED AND RESTRICTED USES GENERALLY[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference- Temporary use of streets for other than public purposes, Code of Virginia, § 15.1-14(9).

Sec. 66-36. - Placing goods, merchandise, wood, coal, etc., on street or sidewalk and permitting same to remain. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to place any goods, wares or merchandise or other property, or cause the same to be placed, in or upon any street or sidewalk and permit the same to remain without first obtaining a permit from the town manager. 
(Code 1968, § 21-5; Ord. of 7-1-2014(3); Ord. of 8-5-2014)
Cross reference- Businesses, ch. 18. 
Sec. 66-37. - Manner of exposure for sale, etc., on sidewalk of goods, merchandise, etc. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to store, keep, expose for show or sale, any goods, wares or other merchandise or property in any gutter or on or over any sidewalk, without first obtaining a permit from the town manager. This section shall not be construed to prohibit permitted mobile food vending authorized under section 66-39. 
(Code 1968, § 21-6; Ord. of 7-1-2014(3); Ord. of 8-5-2014)
Sec. 66-38. - Congregating so as to hinder passage of persons. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to congregate upon any crossing or sidewalk in such manner as to hinder or obstruct the passage of other persons desiring to use the same. 
(Code 1968, § 21-7; Ord. of 8-5-2014)
Sec. 66-39. - Mobile food vending. 
    The town manager or his agent is authorized to issue mobile food vending permits to authorize the placement of a mobile food unit on public right-of-way. "Mobile food unit" means a mobile truck, chuck wagon, food trailer, food cart, or pushcart, and does not imply automobiles, trucks, or vans not designed for food preparation. The following shall apply to mobile food vending: 
(a)	A vending permit shall be revocable with or without cause at the discretion of the town manager or his agent. The permit shall be renewed annually, having the same due date as business licenses. 
(b)	Application for mobile food vending shall be made on permit forms provided by the town manager and the application packet shall include a vending site plan, the width of the sidewalk or parking space utilized, dimensions and a photograph of the unit, a diagram of signage to be utilized, certificate of insurance, and copy of a permit issued by the health department. 
(c)	The mobile food vendor shall conform to town requirements pertaining to business license, meals tax, and other applicable fees and taxes required to operate a food business within the town limits. An applicable permit fee shall accompany the application, and is subject to change. 
(Ord. of 8-5-2014)
Sec. 66-40. - Mobile food vending requirements. 
    Mobile food vending sites shall meet the following requirements: 
(a)	A mobile food vending site shall be located no closer than 100 feet from any public entrance to an eating establishment. 
(b)	Where vending occurs on a sidewalk, at least 36 inches shall remain unobstructed. Business conducted at the mobile food vending location shall not cause the obstruction of vehicular or pedestrian passage. 
(c)	The mobile food unit shall be accompanied by an approved trash receptacle and the area around the unit shall be kept free of trash. Publicly-owned trash receptacles are not approved for use by mobile food vendors. 
(d)	The mobile food unit shall abide by all parking requirements and time limitations.
(e)	Vending transactions shall be limited to pedestrians.
(f)	In the case of an emergency, the mobile food unit shall be removed at the request of a police officer or other emergency official. 
(g)	Radio or sound-amplifying devices, flashing signs, sale of merchandise other than food, water, sewer, electrical, or gas connection to a building or other public utility, or the discharge of pollutants to include waste, grease, liquid, gray water, or debris are prohibited. Signage and appearance of the mobile food vending unit shall be appropriate for the neighborhood in which it is operating. 
(Ord. of 8-5-2014)
Secs. 66-41-66-65. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - EXCAVATIONS 

Sec. 66-66. - Permit required. 
    No person, unless specially authorized by the council, shall take up or remove any portion of the surface of the sidewalk or street, or excavate in any public street of the town, without a written permit from the town manager, who shall not refuse such permit to any applicant except for cause, but in case of refusal the applicant may appeal to the council. 
(Code 1968, § 21-9)
Sec. 66-67. - Deposits; acquiescence in provisions of article. 
(a)	Before a permit as required in section 66-66 is granted, the town manager may require a deposit sufficient to pay for resurfacing the street to be disturbed, the amount of such deposit to be determined by the town manager. 
(b)	Every person who shall make application for such a permit shall be deemed to have assented thereby to all the provisions and terms of this article, including the right of the town to collect the actual cost of replacing the pavement, sidewalk or street surface in the manner above directed. 
(Code 1968, § 21-10)
Sec. 66-68. - Duty to prosecute work without delay. 
    It shall be the duty of every person to whom a permit, as required in section 66-66, shall have been granted, to institute at once and prosecute without delay the work for which such permit was obtained, and promptly on its completion to give written notice thereof to the town manager. 
(Code 1968, § 21-11)
Sec. 66-69. - Replacing surface. 
    No pavement, sidewalk or street surface shall be replaced, after being taken up pursuant to a permit as required in section 66-66, by any person except under the direction of the town manager. If the applicant fails to resurface the street disturbed promptly and in a manner approved by the town manager, the town manager is authorized to cause such work to be done at the expense of the applicant. 
(Code 1968, § 21-12)
Sec. 66-70. - Guarding by lights and barriers; responsible for damages caused by excavation. 
    Any person to whom a permit, as required in section 66-66, is granted shall place guards or barriers around the excavation in question and shall protect it by warning lights at night, and shall be responsible for damages to persons or property caused by such excavations until taken in charge by the town manager. 
(Code 1968, § 21-13)
Sec. 66-71. - Article not applicable to work done by town. 
    The provisions of this article shall not apply to work done by town forces under the supervision of the town manager. 
(Code 1968, § 21-14)
Secs. 66-72-66-79. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - USE OF PUBLIC RIGHTS-OF-WAY 

Sec. 66-80. - Imposition of public rights-of-way use fee. 
    There is imposed upon all certificated providers of telecommunications service occupying the public rights-of-way of the town, a fee in accordance with Code of Virginia of 1950, § 56-468.1, as amended. 
(Ord. of 4-3-2001)
Chapter 70 - SUBDIVISIONS[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Buildings and building regulations, ch. 14; businesses, ch. 18; manufactured homes and trailers, ch. 42; planning, ch. 54; streets, sidewalks and other public places, ch. 66; utilities, ch. 82; zoning, ch. 90; general district provisions for F-C floodplain conservation district, § 90-336; signs in residential districts, § 90-383.
State Law reference- Codification of subdivision ordinance, Code of Virginia, § 15.1-37.3; land subdivision and development, Code of Virginia, § 15.1-465 et seq.; Virginia Public Records Act, Code of Virginia, § 42.1-76 et seq.

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 70-1. - Definitions. 
    For the purposes of this chapter, the following words and phrases shall have the meanings respectively ascribed to them by this section: 
    Administrator means the representative of the town council who has been appointed by the town council to serve as the agent of the council for the administration of this chapter. The administrator may be, but is not limited to, the town clerk or the town manager, town superintendent, town secretary, etc., if officially designated as such. 
    Alley means a permanent service way providing a secondary means of vehicular access to the side or rear of abutting properties and not intended for general traffic circulation. 
    Applicant means the owner of land proposed to be subdivided or his representative authorized in writing; a subdivider. 
    Architect means a person licensed to practice as such in the state. 
    Arterial means a road designated as such by the state department of transportation. 
    Bearings means an angular direction measured from one position to another using reference lines. 
    Block means a tract of land bounded by streets, or by a combination of streets and public parks, cemeteries, railroad rights-of-way, shorelines of waterways or boundary lines of municipalities. 
    Bond means any form of security including a cash deposit, surety bond, collateral, property or instrument of credit in an amount and form satisfactory to the governing body. All bonds shall be approved by the town's attorney whenever a bond is required by this chapter. 
    Building means any structure built for the support, shelter or enclosure of persons, animals, chattels or movable property of any kind, including any structure. 
    Building, main means a building or structure in which the principal use of a lot is carried out. 
    Building (setback) line means the minimum distance of a building from the front boundary line or front lot line. 
    Clerk means the clerk of the circuit court of the county. 
    Collector road means a road determined by the state department of transportation as being a collector road. 
    Commission means the planning commission of the town. 
    Comprehensive plan means the town's comprehensive plan. 
    Council means the town council. 
    Cul-de-sac means a local street with only one outlet and having an appropriate turnaround for a safe and convenient reverse traffic movement. 
    Dedication means the deliberate appropriation of land by its owner for any general or public use, reserving to himself no other rights than those that are compatible with the full exercise and enjoyment of the public uses to which the property has been devoted. 
    Easement means an authorization by a property owner of any designated part of his property for use by another for a specified purpose. 
    Endorsement means the application of the reviewing or approving authority's stamp and the signature of the appropriate authority on the record plat. 
    Engineer means a person licensed to practice as such in the state. 
    Final plat means the final map or plan of a subdivision and any accompanying material, as described in this chapter. 
    Functional classification means a classification of roads, established by the state department of transportation to determine the function of such roads. 
    Governing body means the town council. 
    Grade means the slope of a road, street or other right-of-way, specified in percentage terms. 
    Half street means a street, generally parallel to and adjacent to a property line, having a lesser right-of-way width than normally required. 
    Health department means the health department of the state. 
    Health officer means the legally designated health authority of the state health department for the county, or his authorized representative. 
    Highway engineer means the resident engineer for the county, employed by the state department of transportation. 
    Highway, limited access, means a freeway or expressway providing a trafficway for through traffic, in respect to which owners or occupants of abutting property or lands and other persons having no legal right to access to or from the same, except at such points and in such manner as may be determined by the state department of transportation. 
    Improvements means all required utilities and facilities as specified in this chapter, including, but not limited to, streets, storm and sanitary sewers and water lines. 
    Individual onsite sewage disposal system means a septic tank, seepage tile sewage disposal system or any other sewage treatment device approved by the state health department. 
    Joint ownership of any type among persons is construed as the same owner. 
    Jurisdiction means the area or territory subject to the legislative control of the governing body. 
    Land surveyor means a person licensed to practice as such in the state. 
    Landscape architect means a person licensed to practice as such in the state. 
    Local road means a road so designated by the state department of transportation. 
    Lot means a tract, plot or portion of a subdivision or other parcel of land intended as a unit for the purpose of transfer of ownership or for building development. 
    Lot, corner, means a lot abutting upon two or more streets at their intersection; the shortest side fronting upon a street shall be considered the front of the lot, and the longest side fronting upon a street shall be considered the side of the lot. 
    Lot, depth of, means the mean horizontal distance between the front and rear lot lines. 
    Lot, interior, means a lot other than a corner lot. 
    Lot of record means a lot which has been recorded among the land records in the office of the clerk of the circuit court of the county. 
    Lot, reverse frontage, means an interior lot having frontage on two streets. 
    Lot, width of, means the mean horizontal distance between the side lot lines. 
    Main building. See "building, main." 
    Monument means a permanent steel pin or iron identifying marker meeting the requirements and specifications of this chapter (see section 7-123). 
    Owner means any person having legal title to or sufficient proprietary interest in the land sought to be subdivided under this chapter. 
    Partial street. See "half street." 
    Performance bond means a bond with surety or cash deposit, approved by the governing body and town attorney, in an amount equal to the full cost of improvements required by this chapter and providing for completion of such improvements within a definite period. See "bond." 
    Planning commission means the planning commission of the town.
