ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 78-1. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Street means the entire width between the boundary lines of every way or place of whatever nature open to the use of the public for purposes of vehicular travel in this town, including streets, alleys and publicly maintained parking lots in the town. 
(Code 1968, § 13-4)
Cross reference- Definitions and rules of construction generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 78-2. - Reserved. 
Editor's note- Ord. of July 1, 2006, repealed § 78-2, which pertained to violations of chapter; penalties and derived from Code 1968, § 13-20; Ord. of July 1, 2003. 
Sec. 78-3. - Adoption of state law. 
    Pursuant to the authority of Section 46.2-1313 of the Code of Virginia of 1950, as amended, all of the provisions and requirements of Title 46.2 and Article 2 (Section 18.2-266, et seq.) of Chapter 7 of Title 18.2 of the Code of Virginia of 1950, as amended, except those provisions which are contained in this chapter and except for those provisions and requirements the violation of which constitutes a felony, and except those provisions and requirements which by their very nature can have no application to or within the town are hereby adopted and incorporated in this chapter by reference and made applicable within the town. Reference to "highways of the state" contained in such provisions and requirements hereby adopted shall be deemed to refer to the streets, highways, and other public ways within the town. Such provisions and requirements are hereby adopted, mutatis mutandis, and made a part of this chapter as fully as though set forth at length herein, and it shall be unlawful for any person, within the town to violate or fail, neglect or refuse to comply with any provision of [Title] 46.2 or of Article 2 of Chapter 7 of Title 18.2 of the Code of Virginia which is adopted by this section; provided, that in no event shall the penalty imposed for the violation of any provision or requirement hereby adopted exceed the penalty imposed for a similar offense under Title 46.2 or under Article 2 of Chapter 7 of Title 18.2 of the Code of Virginia of 1950, as amended. 
(Code 1968, § 13-42; Ord. of 7-2-91(1), § 13-42; Ord. No. 467, 7-7-92; Ord. of 7-6-93(1); Ord. of 7-5-94; Ord. of 7-11-95; Ord. of 7-2-96(2); Ord. of 7-1-97(1); Ord. of 7-1-97(2); Ord. of 6-2-2009; Ord. of 6-1-2010; Ord. of 6-7-2011; Ord. of 6-5-2012; Ord. of 6-4-2013; Ord. of 6-3-2014; Ord. of 6-2-2015) 
Sec. 78-4. - Powers and duties of town manager-Traffic and parking generally. 
(a)	The town manager, except as otherwise provided by this chapter and except as otherwise directed from time to time by the council, is hereby authorized to: 
(1)	Regulate the operation and parking of vehicles within the corporate limits of the town by the erection or placing of proper signs or markers indicating prohibited or limited parking, angle parking, the parking of buses, trucks and other vehicles of various weights, U-turns, turning at intersections, hazardous intersections, school zones, hospital zones, loading and unloading zones, quiet zones, traffic control signals exhibiting colored lights or the words "go", "caution" or "stop" and other signs or markers indicating the place and manner of operating or parking vehicles in the town. 
(2)	Regulate the movement of pedestrians upon the streets and sidewalks of the town by the erection or placing of proper signs or markers indicating the flow of pedestrian traffic. 
(3)	Designate bus stops and erect signs prohibiting the parking of vehicles other than buses at such stops. 
(4)	Mark off traffic lanes on streets and parts of streets indicating and directing the flow of traffic. 
(b)	The town manager is hereby authorized to secure all such necessary signs, signals or markers to be erected or placed on any street or part of a street. 
(c)	The existence of such signs, signals or markers at any place within the corporate limits of the town shall be prima facie evidence that such signs, signals or markers were erected or placed by and at the direction of the town manager in accordance with the provisions of this section. 
(Code 1968, § 13-7)
Cross reference- Administration, ch. 2. 
State Law reference- Power of town to delegate authority to make parking regulations, Code of Virginia, § 46.2-220. 
Sec. 78-5. - Same-Stop and yield intersections. 
(a)	The town manager, except as otherwise provided by this chapter and except as otherwise directed from time to time by the council, may designate intersections, other than intersections at which one or more of the intersecting streets has been designated as a part of the state highway system, at which vehicles shall come to a full stop or yield the right-of-way. 
(b)	The town manager is hereby authorized to secure all such necessary signs, signals or markers to be erected or placed on or at any such intersection, so that an ordinarily observant person, who may be affected by such regulation, may be aware of such regulation. 
(c)	The existence of such signs, signals or markers at any place within the corporate limits of the town shall be prima facie evidence that such signs, signals or markers were erected or placed by and at the direction of the town manager in accordance with the provisions of this section. 
(d)	The town manager is hereby authorized to require that stop lines and stop signs be placed by the owners of properties in commercial districts as set forth in section 90-384(c). 
(Code 1968, § 13-8; Ord. of 2-5-91(2), § 13-8)
Sec. 78-6. - Compliance with signs, etc., erected or placed pursuant to section 78-4 or 78-5. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to fail or refuse to comply with the directions indicated on any sign, signal or marker erected or placed in accordance with the provisions of section 78-4 or 78-5 when such sign, signal or marker so placed or erected is visible and legible. 
(Code 1968, § 13-9)
Secs. 78-7-78-9. - Reserved. 
Editor's note- Ord. of July 1, 2006, repealed §§ 78-7-78-9, which pertained to authority of police with reference to traffic; authority of members of fire department to direct traffic; signs prerequisite to enforcement of chapter and regulations, respectively, and derived from Code 1968, §§ 13-21, 13-27, 13-22, respectively; Ord. of July 1, 2003. 
Sec. 78-10. - Legal holidays. 
    For the purposes of this chapter, the following days shall be legal holidays on the respective dates as such holidays are observed, together with any other such days as shall be specified by the town council at its discretion: 
All state and federal holidays. 
(Code 1968, § 13-103.1; Ord. of 7-1-2003; Ord. of 7-1-2006; Ord. of 9-2-2014)
Sec. 78-11. - Traffic violation notices. 
(a)	Traffic violation notices shall be issued to violators of parking regulations and all other nonmoving regulations, with the exception of persons charged with parking too close to or in front of fire hydrants and fire stations and with the further exception of persons charged with parking meter violations, unless circumstances warrant other action, in which event the usual procedure of summons or arrest shall apply. 
(b)	Parking violation notices may be settled by a payment within a period of five days after issuance, of a minimum penalty of $10.00, which payment shall be in complete satisfaction of the offense. Payment shall be made to such person at the town office as from time to time shall be designated by the town manager to receive such payment. Failure to settle a parking violation notice as above provided shall subject the recipient to the penalty as set forth in section 78-81. 
(c)	The town manager shall establish a full and complete procedure for handling traffic violation notices. 
(d)	All amounts paid under this section shall be credited to and become a part of the general fund of the town. 
(Code 1968, § 13-10; Ord. of 7-1-2003; Ord. of 7-1-2006)
Cross reference- Fire prevention and protection, ch. 30. 
Sec. 78-12. - Permits for parades and processions. 
    No parade, excepting the forces of the United States Army or Navy, the military forces of the state and the forces of the police and fire departments of the town, shall occupy or march or proceed along any street, except in accordance with a permit issued by the town manager. 
(Code 1968, § 13-11)
Cross reference- Fire prevention and protection, ch. 30; law enforcement, ch. 38; streets, sidewalks and other public places, ch. 66. 
Secs. 78-13-78-15. - Reserved. 
Editor's note- Ord. of July 1, 2003, repealed §§ 78-13-78-15, which pertained to valid state license plate prerequisite to driving, etc., vehicle on street; valid inspection sticker prerequisite to driving, etc., vehicle on street; tailgates on vehicles, respectively, and derived from Code 1968, §§ 13-13, 13-14, 13-162, respectively. 
Sec. 78-16. - Operating motor vehicles so as to cause noise or provoke breach of peace. 
    No person shall operate a motor vehicle over the streets of the town in a manner causing unnecessary noise or in any other manner reasonably calculated to provoke a breach of the peace. Any person violating this section shall be guilty of a class 4 misdemeanor. 
(Code 1968, § 14-34)
Sec. 78-17. - Reckless riding of skateboards, etc., prohibited. 
    Reckless use of roller skates, skateboards, toys, or other devices on wheels or runners, is prohibited. 
(Code 1968, § 14-27.1)
Sec. 78-18. - Riding bicycles, etc. on sidewalks, etc., prohibited. 
    Riding of bicycles, skateboards, rollerblades, rollerskates, toys, or other devices on wheels or runners, on sidewalks or crosswalks, including those of any church, school, recreational facility, or any business property open to the public is prohibited. Any person violating this section shall, upon conviction, be fined not less than $5.00 nor more than $25.00. 
(Code 1968, § 14-27; Ord. of 6-6-95; Ord. of 6-3-97(2))
Sec. 78-19. - Riding horses, etc., on sidewalks prohibited. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to wilfully ride a horse, mule or other animal upon any sidewalk of the town. Any person violating the provisions of this section shall be guilty of a class 4 misdemeanor. 
(Code 1968, § 14-26; Ord. of 7-2-91(4), § 14-26)
Sec. 78-20. - Driving around rotary traffic islands. 
    A vehicle passing around a rotary traffic island shall be driven only to the right of such island. 
(Ord. of 8-1-2006)
Editor's note- Formerly, Ord. of July 1, 2003, repealed § 78-20, which pertained to railroad cars obstructing street or road; standing vehicle on railroad track and derived from Code 1968, § 13-91. 
State Law reference- Similar provisions, Code of Virginia, § 46.1-204. 
Secs. 78-21-78-40. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - LICENSING AND REGISTRATION[2] 
Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference- Titling and registration of motor vehicles, Code of Virginia, § 46.2-600 et seq.

DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Secs. 78-41-78-50. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - LOCAL VEHICLE LICENSE[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
State Law reference- Local licensing of vehicles, Code of Virginia, § 46.2-752 et seq.

Sec. 78-51. - Imposition of license taxes generally. 
    There is hereby imposed an annual license tax upon the following motor vehicles, trailers and semitrailers, except as otherwise provided in this article: 
(1)	Motor vehicles, trailers, and semitrailers that are normally garaged, stored or parked in the town. 
(2)	If it cannot be determined where the personal property is normally garaged, stored, or parked, or if the owner is a student attending an institution of higher education, motor vehicles and semitrailers whose owner has his domicile in the town. 
(Code 1968, § 13-34)
State Law reference- Situs for the imposition of license taxes, Code of Virginia, § 46.2-752. 
Sec. 78-52. - Amounts of license taxes. 
    The license tax imposed in section 78-51 shall be in the following annual amounts: 
(1)	For motor vehicles, trailers and semitrailers designed and used for the transportation of passengers, other than motorcycles .....$25.00 
(2)	For motor vehicles, trailers and semitrailers not designed for living quarters .....25.00 
(3)	For trailers, semitrailers and camping-type trailers designed for living quarters .....25.00 
(4)	For motorcycles, motorbikes, mopeds and motor scooters .....18.00 
(Code 1968, § 13-35; Ord. of 3-5-91, § 13-35)
Sec. 78-53. - Exemptions. 
    The license taxes imposed in section 78-51 shall not be imposed when: 
(1)	The motor vehicle, trailer or semitrailer is owned by a nonresident and is used for transporting into and within the town for sale in person or by his employees, of wood, meats, poultry, fruits, flowers, vegetables, milk, butter, cream or eggs produced or grown by him, and not purchased by him for sale. 
(2)	The motor vehicle, trailer or semitrailer is kept by a dealer or manufacturer for sale or for sales demonstration. 
(3)	The motor vehicle, trailer or semitrailer is operated by a common carrier of persons or property operating between cities and towns in the state and not in intracity transportation or between cities and towns on the one hand and points and places without cities and towns on the other and not intracity transportation. 
(Code 1968, § 13-36)
State Law reference- Limitations on imposition of motor vehicle license taxes and fees, Code of Virginia, § 46.2-755. 
Sec. 78-54. - When and where license taxes payable; town automobile license tags or stickers generally. 
    The license taxes imposed in section 78-51 shall be payable at the office of the town treasurer before the operation of the motor vehicle, trailer, or semitrailer in question over the streets of the town, and annually thereafter, as provided in this chapter, at which time the owner thereof shall obtain a town automobile license plate or sticker. In the case of a license plate, it shall be securely fastened to the motor vehicle, trailer or semitrailer to which it is assigned, on the rear of trailers or semitrailers, and on either the front or rear of other motor vehicles, in a position to be clearly visible, and in a condition to be clearly legible. 
(Code 1968, § 13-37)
State Law reference- Placement of sticker or decal, Code of Virginia, § 46.2-1052. 
Sec. 78-55. - Transfer of license sticker. 
    The treasurer shall charge a fee of $1.00 for the transfer or reissue of a license sticker within the license year and before any transfer or reissue is made, the treasurer shall require presentation of the receipt for the original sticker and the remains of the original sticker. 
(Code 1968, § 13-37.1)
Sec. 78-56. - License year. 
    The license year under this division shall begin on March 1 of each year and end on February 28 or 29 of the following year. 
(Code 1968, § 13-38; Ord. of 4-7-98)
State Law reference- Period of imposition of license fees, Code of Virginia, § 46.2-752. 
Sec. 78-57. - Purchase of license tags by new residents. 
    New residents of the town shall have 30 days in which to purchase automobile license tags. 
(Code 1968, § 13-38.1)
Sec. 78-58. - Proration of license tax. 
    One-half of the annual license tax prescribed in this division shall be collected whenever any town automobile license tax is obtained during the period beginning on August 15 in any year, and ending on December 1 in the same license year, and one-third of such annual license tax shall be collected whenever any town automobile license tag is obtained after January 15 in any license year. 
(Code 1968, § 13-39; Ord. of 4-7-98)
State Law reference- Manner of proration of license fees, Code of Virginia, § 46.2-752. 
Sec. 78-59. - Payment of personal property tax prerequisite to issuance of license. 
    No motor vehicle, trailer or semitrailer shall be licensed by the town unless and until the applicant for such license shall have produced evidence satisfactory to the town that all personal property taxes upon the motor vehicle, trailer or semitrailer have been paid, which have been properly assessed or are assessable against the applicant by the town. 
(Code 1968, § 13-40)
Cross reference- Taxation, ch. 74. 
State Law reference- Authority for above section, Code of Virginia, § 46.2-752. 
Sec. 78-60. - Penalty for violation of article. 
    Any person violating the provisions of this article shall be guilty of a class 4 misdemeanor for each offense. 
(Code 1968, § 13-41)
Sec. 78-61. - Exemption of volunteers. 
    Each active volunteer member of a volunteer fire department or volunteer rescue squad who appears as an official member of such organization on their respective departmental roster or roll, shall receive an annual license for one vehicle free of charge. 
(Ord. of 1-2-2001)
Secs. 78-62-78-80. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - STOPPING, STANDING AND PARKING[4] 
Footnotes: 
--- (4) --- 
Charter reference- Adoption of Code of Virginia, § 15.1-884, pertaining to parking or storage of vehicles, § 4.
Cross reference- Offstreet parking, § 90-387 et seq.

DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 78-81. - Penalties for violations. 
    Except where otherwise specifically provided, any person violating the provisions of this chapter, or aiding, abetting or assisting in the violation of such provisions, shall, upon conviction, be fined as follows: 
(1)	Overtime parking .....$10.00 
(2)	On or blocking a sidewalk; blocking a public or private driveway; blocking a public or private alley or driveway; on or across a pedestrian crosswalk .....20.00 
(3)	On the roadway side of any vehicle parked at the edge or curb of street, this violation being known as double parking .....20.00 
(4)	In a restricted zone where such zones are marked with official signs, except posted parking areas .....20.00 
(5)	Commercial vehicle in residential district (Town Code) .....20.00 
(6)	On the wrong side of street (left wheel to curb) against traffic .....20.00 
(7)	Across marked lines of a parking space .....20.00 
(8)	Over or on top of curb .....20.00 
(9)	Handicap violation .....50.00 
(Code 1968, § 13-112; Ord. of 7-1-2003; Ord. of 7-1-2006)
Sec. 78-82. - Moving vehicle into prohibited area, etc. 
    No person other than a police officer shall move a vehicle into any prohibited area, as provided for in Code of Virginia, § 46.2-1239, or away from a curb such distance as is unlawful. 
(Code 1968, § 13-95)
Secs. 78-83, 78-84. - Reserved. 
Editor's note- Ord. of July 1, 2003, repealed §§ 78-83, 78-84, which pertained to backing up to curbs; unauthorized parking in taxicab stands, respectively, and derived from Code 1968, §§ 13-100, 13-101, respectively. 
Sec. 78-85. - Commercial vehicles-Parking in residential zones and/or any public right-of-way prohibited. 
(a)	It shall be unlawful for any person to park a commercial vehicle in any residential zone and/or any public right-of-way. 
(b)	The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this section, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Commercial vehicle means: 
(1)	Any solid waste collection vehicle, tractor truck or tractor truck/semitrailer or tractor truck/trailer combination (or any part thereof), dump truck, concrete mixer truck, towing and recovery vehicle, box type truck, step van, panel truck, flat bed truck, or heavy construction equipment, whether located on private property or on a truck, trailer or semitrailer; 
(2)	Any trailer, semitrailer, or other vehicle in which food or beverages are stored or sold; 
(3)	Any motor vehicle licensed by the commonwealth for use as a common or contract carrier or as a limousine, to include school buses; 
(4)	Any other trailer used for commercial purposes; or
(c)	Any person who violates this section shall be punished by a fine not exceeding $100.00.
(d)	This section shall not apply to parking in the course of legitimate deliveries or service calls. 
(Code 1968, § 13-19.1; Ord. of 7-1-2003; Ord. of 7-6-2004; Ord. of 7-1-2006)
Cross reference- Definitions and rules of construction generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 78-86. - Reserved. 
Editor's note- Ord. of July 1, 2003, repealed § 78-86, which pertained to tractor trucks and semitrailers-starting tractor trucks in residential zones and derived from Code 1968, § 13-19.2. 
Sec. 78-87. - Parking of vendors and peddlers prohibited. 
(a)	It shall be unlawful for any person to park any vehicle on the public streets, highways, sidewalks or public areas of the town for the purpose of vending or peddling goods or merchandise of any kind. A violation of this section shall be punishable by a fine of not more than $100.00. 
(b)	The provisions of this section shall not apply to vending during a recognized public event having the prior approval of a town permit. 
(Ord. No. 463, 4-7-92; Ord. of 9-2-2014)
Cross reference- Peddlers generally, § 18-121 et seq.; vending and peddling prohibited on public property, § 46-27.1 
Sec. 78-88. - Stopping on streets; generally. 
(a)	No vehicle shall be stopped in such manner as to impede or render dangerous the use of the street by others, except in the case of an emergency as the result of an accident or mechanical breakdown, in which case a report shall be made to the nearest police officer as soon as practicable and the vehicle shall be removed from the roadway to the shoulder without unnecessary delay; and, if such vehicle is not promptly removed, such removal may also be ordered by a police officer at the expense of the owner if the disabled vehicle creates a traffic hazard. 
(b)	No vehicle shall be stopped except close to and parallel to the right-hand edge of the curb or roadway, except that a vehicle may be stopped close to and parallel to the left-hand curb or edge of the roadway on one-way streets or may be parked at an angle where permitted by the state highway commission or chief of police with respect to streets and highways under their respective jurisdictions. 
(c)	No vehicle shall be stopped at or in the vicinity of a fire, vehicle or airplane accident or other area of emergency, in such a manner as to create a traffic hazard or interfere with the necessary procedures of police, firemen, rescue workers or others whose duty it is to deal with such emergencies. Any vehicle found unattended in the vicinity of such fire, accident or area of emergency may be removed by order of a police officer at the risk and expense, not to exceed $50.00, of the owner if such vehicle creates a traffic hazard or interferes with the necessary procedures of police, firemen, rescue workers or others whose assigned duty it is to deal with such emergencies. Vehicles being used by accredited information services, such as press, radio and television, when being used for the gathering of news, shall be exempt from the provisions of this section, except when actually obstructing the police, firemen and rescue workers dealing with such emergencies. 
(Ord. of 7-6-93)
Sec. 78-89. - Penalty for overtime parking in 15 minute and two hour parking zones. 
(a)	If any vehicle shall remain parked in a 15 minute or two hour parking zone in excess of 15 minutes or two hours, respectively, it shall be considered as parking overtime, and the parking of such vehicle overtime shall be unlawful. Each violator receiving a ticket noting such violation may, within 24 hours of the time when such ticket notice was attached to such vehicle, pay at the town treasurer's office or the police department, the sum of $10.00 for and in full satisfaction of such violation. In lieu of making such payment at the town treasurer's office or police department, the requisite sum may be deposited in the envelopes provided in one of the yellow Traf-O-Teria Courtesy Boxes located on certain posts within the period of 24 hours. The failure of such violator to make such payment to the town treasure or police department in one of these methods provided herein within 24 hours shall result in a fine of $20.00, and the police department shall notify such violator by letter that the fine is $20.00. 
(b)	The failure of such violator to make such payment of $10.00 to the town treasurer within five days of the date of such letter shall result in a summons being issued in accordance with Code of Virginia, § 46.2-941, and shall render such violator subject to the penalties provided under section 78-81. 
(c)	The owner or operator of any vehicle parked in violation of this section shall be prima facie guilty of such violation. 
(d)	The 15 minute and two-hour parking zone restrictions shall apply Monday thru Saturday, except Holidays, from 8:00 a.m. until 5:00 p.m. 
(Ord. of 11-2-93(1); Ord. of 11-7-2000; Ord. of 7-1-2003; Ord. of 7-1-2006; Ord. of 8-2-2006) 
Sec. 78-90. - Penalties for continuous violations of two hour and 15 minute limit parking. 
    Any violation of two hour parking, and 15 minute limited parking in excess of three within any 30-day period, shall be punished by a fine of $10.00 if paid within 21 days of the mailing of a letter by the police department to the violator notifying the violator of this offense. If the sum of $10.00 is not paid within the 21-day period, the fine shall be $25.00. 
(Ord. of 11-7-2000)
Secs. 78-91-78-95. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - EMERGENCY ROUTES[5] 

Footnotes:

Sec. 78-96. - Emergency routes designated. 
    The following streets within the town are hereby designed emergency routes: 
(1)	Both sides of Mill Road from North Water Street to US Route 11 (North Main Street). 
(2)	Both sides of West North Street from US Route 11 to Norfolk Southern Railroad right-of-way. 
(3)	North side of West North Street from Norfolk Southern Railroad right-of-way to Summit Avenue. 
(4)	Both sides of West North Street from Summit Avenue north to US I-81 overpass.
(5)	North side of West Spring Street from US Route 11 to Summit Avenue. 
(6)	Both sides of Massanutten Heights.
(7)	Both sides of Ox Road from Park Avenue to corporate limits just south of Southridge Court. 
(8)	Both sides of Indian Spring Road from US Route 11 to South Water Street. 
(9)	Both sides of Hollingsworth Road from South Water Street to Eagle Street.
(10)	Both sides of Hollingsworth Road from Lupton Road to Lincoln Street.
(11)	Both sides of Lupton Road from Hollingsworth Road to Corporate Limits.
(12)	Both sides of East Reservoir Road from US Route 11 to entrance road to Aston Properties shopping center. 
(Ord. of 11-12-2003)
Sec. 78-97. - Parking prohibited at all times. 
    Parking is prohibited at all times on all streets designated as emergency routes in section 78-96. 
(Ord. of 11-12-2003)
Sec. 78-98. - Signs. 
    All "No Parking" signs posted pursuant to this section, shall be placed and erected by the town and shall conform to those erected for similar purpose by the department of transportation. 
(Ord. of 11-12-2003)
Sec. 78-99. - Removal and storage of vehicles in violation. 
    Upon information that a vehicle is parked, stalled, stuck or abandoned on any emergency route designated by this division, the chief of police shall authorize immediate removal and storage of such vehicle. 
(Ord. of 11-12-2003)
Sec. 78-100. - Costs of removal and storage. 
    The costs of removing and storing any vehicles towed or otherwise removed under section 78-99, shall be charged to the owner and shall be due and payable prior to any such release of the vehicle to the owner. 
(Ord. of 11-12-2003)
Sec. 78-101. - Violation. 
    Any person convicted of violating any provision of this division shall be filed not more that $50.00 for each violation. 
(Ord. of 11-12-2003)
Secs. 78-102-78-125. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - BICYCLES 

Sec. 78-126. - Registration of bicycles. 
    Every resident of the town owning a bicycle shall, within ten days of the purchase of each bicycle, apply to the chief of police for a registration tag without cost to the owner. Such application shall contain the make, description and serial number of each bicycle. The bicycle registration tag shall at all times be securely fastened to the bicycle in a conspicuous place. 
(Code 1968, § 3.1-1)
Sec. 78-127. - Disposition of unclaimed bicycles. 
    The police department may sell at public sale or may donate to a charitable organization any bicycle which has been in the possession of the police department, unclaimed, for more than 30 days. Any bicycle found and delivered to the police department by a private person which thereafter remains unclaimed for 60 days after the final date of publication as required in this section may be given to the finder. There shall be published at least once a week for two successive weeks in a newspaper of general circulation within the town the location and description of the bicycle; and, in addition, if there is a license tag affixed to the bicycle, the record owner shall be notified directly. 
(Code 1968, § 3.1-2)
Secs. 78-128-78-150. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - ACCIDENTS 

Sec. 78-151. - Filing of accident reports-Required; copies. 
    The driver of any vehicle involved in an accident must file with the police department a report of the accident or a copy of any report required to be filed with the state department of motor vehicles. All such reports shall be for the confidential use of the police department, except, however, any such reports, including the report of the police officer, and including such photographs taken by inspection by any person involved or injured in the accident or his attorney or any authorized representative of any insurance carrier reasonably anticipating exposure to civil liability as a consequence of the accident. Each copy of any such report and each copy of any such photograph shall be furnished to any such person, attorney or authorized representative upon the payment of a fee that the council may from time to time determine by general resolution, for each such copy. 
(Code 1968, § 13-181.1; Ord. of 6-1-2010)
Sec. 78-152. - Same-Penalty. 
    Any person convicted of violating the provisions of section 78-151 shall, if such accident results in injury to or the death of, any person or damage to property, be guilty of a class 1 misdemeanor; however, if the vehicle or other property struck is unattended and such damage is less than $250.00, such person shall be guilty of a class 4 misdemeanor. 
(Code 1968, § 13-182)
State Law reference- Similar provisions, Code of Virginia, § 46.2-900.

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 82-1. - Superintendent of public works generally; definition of "superintendent." 
(a)	There is hereby created the position of superintendent of public works. The superintendent shall be appointed by the town manager, to serve at the pleasure of the town manager. 
(b)	The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Superintendent means the superintendent of public works or his duly authorized representative. 
(Code 1968, § 27-1)
Cross reference- Definitions and rules of construction generally, § 1-2; administration, ch. 2. 
Secs. 82-2-82-25. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - WATER SYSTEM; CHARGES FOR WATER AND SEWER SERVICE[2] 
Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Cross reference- Water supply in subdivisions, § 70-117.

DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 82-26. - Powers and duties of superintendent generally. 
(a)	In addition to his duties of laying down pipes, erecting fire hydrants or any other work necessary to be done in connection with the waterworks, the superintendent shall be in charge of the entire water supply system and shall have a general control of all lands, buildings, reservoirs, dams, pipelines and machinery belonging thereto, and shall be responsible for the proper operation of same. 
(b)	Generally, the superintendent shall supervise the maintenance and operation of the town water system and shall have such other duties in connection therewith as may be prescribed by the council. 
(Code 1968, § 27-2)
Cross reference- Fire prevention and protection, ch. 30. 
Sec. 82-27. - Reserved. 
Editor's note- Ord. of October 8, 2014, repealed § 82-27, entitled "Map of location, etc., of mains; records as to valves, taps, etc." and derived from Code 1968, § 27-3. 
Sec. 82-28. - Right of entry of superintendent, etc. 
    Every person occupying any lot or tenement into which water is conducted under this article shall permit the superintendent or his agent, or any authorized agent of this town, to enter such lot or tenement at reasonable hours to inspect the works therein or to see if this article has been violated. 
(Code 1968, § 27-4)
Sec. 82-29. - Reserved. 
Editor's note- Ord. of October 8, 2014, repealed § 82-29, entitled "Superintendent to purchase materials, etc., keep records and make monthly report" and derived from Code 1968, § 27-5. 
Sec. 82-30. - Reserved. 
Editor's note- Ord. of October 8, 2014, repealed § 82-30, entitled "Book of, and procedure as to, requests for introduction of water upon premises" and derived from Code 1968, § 27-6. 
Sec. 82-31. - Duty of property owner upon issuance of permit for introduction of water to premises; limitations on introduction of water to premises. 
(a)	Whenever upon application of the property owner, as provided for in section 82-30, a permit for introduction of town water has been issued by the superintendent, the owner of the premises shall lay down the pipe conveying the water from the curb in the street into and upon the premises, and the manner of such connection shall be governed by this division. 
(b)	No water shall be introduced upon any premises except through such service pipe and through the water meter to be installed in connection therewith by the superintendent. 
(c)	There shall be a separate service pipe and meter for each extension used by a different family or tenant upon the same premises, and in no case shall water hereafter be introduced into two or more houses or tenements through one curb stop; except, that in the case of apartments or other multiple-family dwellings, the town manager, at his discretion, may authorize the installation of a master meter. 
(Code 1968, § 27-7)
Sec. 82-32. - Issuance of connection permit; procedure for making of connection by plumber. 
    Upon compliance with the applicable conditions and the payment of a charge in an amount to be fixed by the council by general resolution the town manager shall issue a written permit granting the privilege of connecting with the town water system upon the terms described by this Code and other ordinances of the town, but the introduction of water shall only be made under the direction of the superintendent and by a properly qualified plumber who shall use such pipe, fixtures and fittings as provided by this Code and other ordinances of the town. 
(Code 1968, § 27-8; Ord. of 10-8-2014)
Sec. 82-33. - Prerequisites to introduction of town water to lot; introduction of corporation stop, etc., to town pipe; laying pipe or breaking surface of street. 
    No person shall, without a written permit from the town manager, or at such time as he cannot be present or properly represented, introduce into any lot or tenement water from the town pipes, or introduce any corporation stop or other fixture into such pipes, or construct or lay down, or have constructed or laid down, any pipes or other works for the purpose of introducing water into a lot or tenement, or break up any street for the purpose of constructing or laying down any such pipes or works. As far as the breaking up of any street for the purpose of constructing or laying down any such pipes or works is concerned, the possession of a permit shall be sufficient. 
(Code 1968, § 27-9; Ord. of 10-8-2014)
Sec. 82-34. - Supply of water through water meters. 
    All water supplied by the town and sold to persons shall be supplied through water meters, which shall be installed by and remain the property of the town. 
(Code 1968, § 27-10)
Sec. 82-35. - Location of curb boxes, etc. 
    In connection with the water supply system, all curb boxes, stops and water meters shall be located at or near the property line from which water is connected. 
(Code 1968, § 27-11; Ord. of 10-8-2014)
Sec. 82-36. - Access to and use of stopcock at curb and water meter. 
    Access to the water meter can only be had by the superintendent. Any person using such water meter for any purpose whatever without the written permission of the superintendent shall be punished as provided in section 1-7. 
(Code 1968, § 27-12; Ord. of 10-8-2014)
Sec. 82-37. - Reserved. 
Editor's note- Ord. of October 8, 2014, repealed § 82-37, entitled "Stopcocks on water service lines on owner's premises" and derived from Code 1968, § 27-13. 
Sec. 82-38. - Injuring pipelines, etc.; unauthorized opening, etc., of fixtures. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to injure, deface or destroy any of the pipelines or any part of the pipelines of the water system of the town, including the main, extending from the town to the raw water, or for any unauthorized person to open, close, injure, deface or destroy any cock, wheel, fireplug, gate, valve gate, flush gate, air valve, water meter or any other fixture connected with or pertaining to the waterworks of the town. For each such offense every person shall be guilty of a class 1 misdemeanor. 
(Code 1968, § 27-14; Ord. of 10-8-2014)
Cross reference- Property damage generally, § 46-16. 
Sec. 82-39. - Pollution or contamination at intakes at mountain reservoirs. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to bathe in, or in any way or manner do anything that will pollute or contaminate the water at the intakes at the mountain reservoirs, or to throw or deposit stones, sticks, or other foreign matter in such water, either at such intakes or in such reservoirs. For each offense every such person shall be guilty of a class 1 misdemeanor. 
(Code 1968, § 27-15)
State Law reference- Power of council to prevent the pollution of water and injury to waterworks, Code of Virginia, § 15.1-292. 
Sec. 82-40. - Use of water in emergencies. 
    In case of prolonged drought or other emergency affecting the water supply or the water system, the town manager may declare a state of emergency and restrict or forbid the use of water from the town water system for nonessential purposes. Notice of such declaration and order shall be disseminated in such manner as he shall deem most practicable. Any person knowingly violating any restrictions imposed under such declaration and order shall be pun ished as provided in section 1-7, and water service to such person's premises may be discontinued if such action is deemed necessary by the town manager. 
(Code 1968, § 27-23)
Secs. 82-41-82-50. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - CHARGES AND BILLS 

Sec. 82-51. - Responsibility of owner of premises for water charges, etc. 
    All water and sewer charges in whatever way or for whatever purposes laid shall be charged against and be made payable by the owner of the premises upon which they are respectively imposed. 
(Code 1968, § 27-16)
Sec. 82-52. - Water rates and deposits; users of water outside town. 
    Water shall be charged for by the town at such rates as the council may from time to time determine by general resolution. The council may also require a deposit, the amount of which shall be established by the council by general resolution, in advance on water rents and charges. Users of water outside the limits of the town may be charged higher rates than those in town, and service to users outside the limits of the town shall be subject to being restricted or discontinued at any time the council may deem such action to be necessary or expedient. 
(Code 1968, § 27-17)
Sec. 82-53. - Charges, etc., for use of sewer system. 
    Charges and deposits shall be made for the use of the town sewer system as the council may from time to time by general resolution direct. Such charges shall be billed and collected by the town treasurer in the same manner as provided for the billing and collecting water charges. Higher rates may be charged out-of-town users of the town sewer system. 
(Code 1968, § 27-18)
Sec. 82-54. - Reading of water meters. 
    The town manager shall cause all water meters to be read once a month and a record of such reading shall be promptly furnished to the town treasurer. 
(Code 1968, § 27-19; Ord. of 3-4-2008; Ord. of 10-8-2014)
Sec. 82-55. - Treasurer to send bills to water users and for sewer charges; when bill payable. 
    The town treasurer shall, as soon as possible after receiving the report of the meter readings, send a bill to each user of water from the town water system. Such bill shall also include any sewer rents and charges against such user and shall be payable immediately upon receipt by such user. 
(Code 1968, § 27-20)
Sec. 82-56. - Multiple business units or family living units on same meter. 
    Where a building with more than one business unit or multifamily living unit is served on the same premises from the same water meter, the minimum, as determined by general resolution of the town council, shall be charged for each business unit or family living unit, and the minimum allowance as determined by general resolution of the town council, shall apply to each minimum charge. 
(Code 1968, § 27-20.1; Ord. of 3-4-2008)
Sec. 82-57. - Procedure in case of failure to pay bill for water or sewer charges. 
    Should any bill for water or sewer charges not be paid by the fifteenth day of the month following the billing date, a penalty of ten percent of the amount of such bill shall be added thereto. Should any such charge for water or sewer remain unpaid after the 25th day of the month following the billing date, the town treasure shall notify the superintendent, who shall cause the water to be stopped from the premises or tenement of the user so in default. When water is cut off for nonpayment of water or sewer charges, all charges in arrears and penalties thereon, plus an additional service charge to be determined by general resolution of the town council, shall be paid to the town treasurer before the supply is turned on again. 
(Code 1968, § 27-21; Ord. of 3-4-2008)
Sec. 82-58. - Use of town water when water has been cut off for failure to pay charges. 
    Any person responsible for the payment of water or sewer charges, who shall, with knowledge that water supplied from the town water system to the premises occupied by him has been cut off for the nonpayment of such charges, use water from such system prior to the time the water is turned on the premises in question by a proper officer of the town, shall be guilty of a class 1 misdemeanor. 
(Code 1968, § 27-22)
Secs. 82-59-82-64. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - WATER SHORTAGES 

Sec. 82-65. - Declaring of an emergency. 
    In order to provide for an adequate supply of potable water during conditions of drought, high usage, contamination or other emergency conditions, the town hereby adopts the following regulations and restrictions on the delivery and use of potable water. 
(Ord. of 9-6-2011; Ord. of 10-8-2014)
Sec. 82-66. - Definitions. 
    The following words and phrases, when used in this division, shall have the meaning ascribed to them below, except in those instances when the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Assessment date: The date of the water bill on which a fine for violation of this division is imposed. 
    Establishing landscaping: Landscaping plantings or lawns existing in an area after such period of time as to accomplish an establishment and maintenance of growth. 
    New landscaping: Any landscaping or lawns made up of plants or seeds planted in or transplanted to an area within such period of time as to accomplish a reasonable establishment and maintenance of growth. This does not include aeration and seeding, dethatching and seeding, or power overseeding of established lawns. 
    Person: Any individual, corporation, partnership, association, company, business, trust, joint venture or other legal entity. 
    Swimming pool: Any structure, basin, chamber, or tank including hot tubs, containing an artificial body of water for swimming, diving or recreational bathing and having a depth of two feet or more at any point. 
    Vegetable garden: Any "non-commercial" vegetable garden planted primarily for household use; "non-commercial" includes incidental direct selling of produce from such a vegetable garden to the public. 
(Ord. of 9-6-2011)
Sec. 82-67. - Mandatory public water use restrictions. 
    The use of the public water system shall be limited as follows: 
(1)	Paved areas. Washing is prohibited except for health and safety requirements. 
(2)	Swimming pools. Filling and replenishing to maintain health and safety is permitted. All other uses are prohibited. 
(3)	Vehicle washing. Non-commercial washing of vehicles is prohibited. Commercial vehicle washing businesses are permitted to operate under normal conditions. 
(4)	Established landscaping, vegetable gardens. Watering is prohibited except for watering by buckets of up to five gallons in size per day. 
(5)	New landscaping. All watering is permitted for the first 30 days after planting. Thereafter, the restriction for established landscaping shall apply. 
(6)	Restaurants. Water shall be served to customers only upon request. 
(7)	All other businesses. Water use is limited to uses essential for business use and human hygiene. 
(8)	Additional provision. Any other restrictions deemed necessary by the town manager. 
(Ord. of 9-6-2011; Ord. of 10-8-2014)
Sec. 82-68. - When restrictions go into effect. 
(a)	The water use restrictions set forth in this division shall take effect when any one or more of the following conditions occurs: 
(1)	Watch - The stream flows fall between the 10th and 25th percentile or the river level is nine inches over the top of the raw water intake pipes. 
Drought potential if conditions persist - Increase water conservation awareness; voluntary actions by citizens. 
(2)	Warning - The stream flows fall between the 5th and 10th percentile or the river level is six inches over the top of the raw water intake pipes. 
Onset of drought is imminent - Water conservation awareness; precautionary measures voluntary but encouraged by locality. 
(3)	Emergency - The stream flows fall below the 5th percentile or the river level is three inches over the top of the raw water intake pipes. 
Mandatory response for water conservation by locality and public - Mandatory restrictions as described in section 82-67. 
(b)	Notice-Notice of these public water use restrictions shall end when the notice that triggered the restrictions is superseded by a notice indicating the reason for the restrictions no longer exists. 
(Ord. of 9-6-2011)
Sec. 82-69. - Notice. 
    Notice of these public water use restrictions shall be published in the newspaper for a period of one day per week each week during which the restrictions are in effect. The town may utilize other methods of notice to supplement the published notice. 
(Ord. of 9-6-2011)
Sec. 82-70. - Violation. 
    It shall be a violation of this division for any person to use water, or allow or cause the use of water, in violation of the provisions of this division after the first publication required by section 82-69 of this division. 
(Ord. of 9-6-2011)
Sec. 82-71. - Penalty. 
(a)	Any person who violates any provision of this division after publication of notice pursuant to section 82-69 above shall be subject to the following penalties: 
(1)	For the first offense, violators shall receive a written warning delivered in person or posted by a representative of the Town of Woodstock. 
(2)	For the second offense, violators shall be fined $50.00, the fine to be imposed on the violator's next water bill. 
(3)	For the third and each subsequent offense, violators shall be fined $100.00 for each offense, the fine to be imposed on the violator's next water bill. 
(4)	Each violation by a person shall be counted as a separate violation by that person, irrespective of the location at which the violation occurs. 
(b)	Persons who have been assessed a penalty shall have the right to challenge the assessment by providing a written notice to the town manager within ten days of the assessment date. The town manager shall determine whether the penalty was properly assessed and notify the complaining person in writing of his determination. 
(c)	The town manager may waive the penalty if he determines that the violation occurred due to no fault of the person. 
(Ord. of 9-6-2011; Ord. of 10-8-2014)
Secs. 82-72-82-80. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - SEWERS AND SEWAGE DISPOSAL[3] 
Footnotes:

III, IV pertained to similar subject matter and derived from Code 1968, §§ 27-24-27-66; Ord. of Dec. 5, 1995; Ord. of Oct. 3, 2006; Ord. of Apr. 3, 2007. Cross reference- Sanitary sewage disposal in subdivisions, § 70-115.
State Law reference- Power of council to construct sewers and drains, Code of Virginia, § 15.1-292; sewage disposal generally, Code of Virginia, § 15.1-317 et seq.; sewage disposal systems, bond issues, Code of Virginia, § 15.1-320 et seq.

DIVISION 1. - DEFINITIONS 

Sec. 82-81. - Specific definitions. 
    Unless the context of usage indicates otherwise, the meaning of specific terms in this article shall be as follows: 
    Act shall mean the Federal Clean Water Act, 33. U.S.C. 1251 et seq. 
    Approval authority means the executive director or director of the department of environmental quality. 
    ASTM shall mean the American Society for Testing and Materials. 
    Authorized representative of industrial user shall mean: 
(1)	A principal executive officer of at least the level of vice president, if the industrial user is a corporation; or 
(2)	A general partner or proprietor if the industrial user is a partnership or sole proprietorship respectively; or 
(3)	A duly authorized representative of the individual designated in subsections (1) or (2), above, if such representative is responsible for the overall operation of the facility from which the discharge to the POTW originates. The authorization must be submitted to the (manager) prior to or together with any reports to be signed by the authorized representative. 
    BOD (denoting biochemical oxygen demand) shall mean the quantity of oxygen used in the biochemical oxidation of organic matter under standard laboratory procedure in five days at 20 degrees Celsius, expressed in milligrams per liter. 
    Building sewer shall mean the extension from a building wastewater plumbing facility to the treatment works. 
    Categorical pretreatment standard or categorical standard shall mean any regulation containing pollutant discharge limits promulgated by the EPA in accordance with Sections 307(a) and 307(c) of the Act, which apply to specific categories of industrial users which appear in 40 CFR Chapter I, Subchapter N, Parts 405 - 471. 
    Combined sewer shall mean a sewer intended to receive both wastewater and storm or surface water. 
    Commercial user (class 3) shall mean all premises used only for commercial purposes and which is connected to the treatment works. 
    Day shall mean the 24-hour period beginning at 12:01 a.m. 
    Discharger shall mean person or persons, firm, company, industry or other similar sources of wastewater who introduce such into the POTW. 
    Easement shall mean an acquired legal right for the specific use of land owned by others. 
    EPA shall mean the United States Environmental Protection Agency. 
    Establishment shall mean any industrial establishment, mill, factory, tannery, paper or pulp mill, mine, coal mine, colliery, breaker or coal processing operations, quarry, oil refinery, boat, vessel, and each and every other industry or plant or works the operation of which produces industrial wastes or other wastes or which may otherwise alter the physical, chemical or biological properties of any state waters. 
    Existing source shall mean any source of discharge, the construction or operation of which commenced prior to the publication of proposed categorical pretreatment standards which will be applicable to such source if the standard is thereafter promulgated in accordance with Section 307 of the Act. 
    Garbage shall mean the solid animal and vegetable wastes resulting from the domestic or commercial handling, storage, dispensing, preparation, cooking, and serving of foods. 
    Grease means melted animal fat; any substance identified as grease per the Environmental Protection Agency method 14003. 
    Grease interceptor means typically a concrete structure with a 500 to 3,000 gallon capacity that is installed outside of the building, and collects waste only from the kitchen area (no sanitary waste). 
    Grease trap means any device installed inside a facility to separate grease from the wastewater. Generally grease traps are installed in kitchens under the floor or next to a sink, and are much smaller than grease interceptors. 
    Ground water shall mean any water beneath the land surface in the zone of saturation. 
    Indirect discharge shall mean the introduction of (nondomestic) pollutants into the POTW from any nondomestic source regulated under Section 307(b) (c) or (d) of the Act. 
    Industrial user or significant discharger means a source of indirect discharge, or a nondomestic discharge to a treatment works. 
    Industrial wastes shall mean liquid or other wastes resulting from any process of industry, manufacture, trade or business, or from the development of any natural resources. 
    Interference shall mean an inhibition or disruption of the POTW, its treatment processes or operations, or its sludge processes, which clearly causes, in whole or in part, a violation of any requirement of the POTW's VPDES permit, including those discharges that prevent the use or disposal of sludge by the POTW in accordance with any federal or state laws, regulations, permits or sludge management plans. 
    Manager shall mean the Town Manager of the Town of Woodstock or an authorized designee. 
    May is permissible; shall is mandatory. 
    Municipality shall mean a city, county, town, district association, authority or other public body created under the law and having jurisdiction over disposal of sewage, industrial, or other wastes. 
    Natural outlet shall mean any outlet into a watercourse, pond, ditch, lake, or any other body of surface or groundwater. 
    New source shall have the same meaning as provided in 40 CFR Part 403.3(k) (1990). 
    Oil means any type of various greasy, combustible substances obtained from animal, vegetable, and mineral sources: oils are liquid at ordinary temperatures and soluble in certain organic solvents, but not in water. 
    Oil water separator means typically an engineered steel tank designed to separate petroleum oil from water through the use of baffled compartments and corrugated plates. 
    Owner shall mean the commonwealth or any of its political subdivisions, including, but not limited to, sanitation district commissions and authorities, and public or private institutions, corporations, associations, firms or companies organized or existing under the laws of this or any other state or country, or any person or group of persons acting individually or as a group. 
    Pass-through shall mean the discharge of pollutants through a POTW into state waters in quantities or concentrations which are a cause in whole or in part of a violation of any requirement of the POTW's VPDES permit, including an increase in the magnitude or duration of a violation. 
    Person shall mean any individual, firm, company, association, society, partnership, corporation, municipality, or other similar organization, agency or group. 
    pH shall mean the logarithm of the reciprocal of the hydrogen ion concentration expressed in grams per liter of solution as determined by standard methods. 
    Pollutant shall mean any dredged spoil, solid waste, incinerator residue, filter backwash, sewage, garbage, sewage sludge, munitions, medical waste, chemical waste, industrial waste, biological materials, radio active material, heat wrecked or discarded equipment, rock, sand, cellar dirt, municipal, agricultural and industrial waste, and certain characteristics of the wastewater (i.e., pH, temperature, TSS, turbidity, color, BOD, COD, toxicity, odor). 
    POTW, publicly owned treatment works shall mean any sewage treatment works that is owned by a state or municipality. Sewers, pipes, or other conveyances are included in this definition only if they convey wastewater to a POTW providing treatment. 
    Pretreatment shall mean the reduction of the amount of pollutants, the elimination of pollutants, or the alteration of the nature of pollutant properties in wastewater prior to discharge to the town's treatment works. 
    Pretreatment requirements shall mean any substantive or procedural requirement related to pretreatment imposed on an industrial user, other than a pretreatment standard. 
    Pretreatment standard shall mean any regulation containing pollutant discharge limits promulgated by the EPA in accordance with Section 307(b) and (c) of the Act, which applies to industrial users. 
    Properly shredded garbages shall mean garbage that has been shredded to such a degree that all particles will be carried freely under flow conditions normally prevailing in the treatment works, with no particle greater than two inch in any dimension. 
    Residential user (Class 1) shall mean all premises used only for human residency and which is connected to the treatment works. 
    Sand interceptor (grit interceptor) means typically a concrete structure installed outside the building designed to collect sand, grit, or other inorganic particles prior to admission to the public sanitary sewer. 
    Sanitary wastewater shall mean wastewater discharged from the sanitary conveniences of dwellings, office buildings, industrial plants, or institutions. 
    Sanitary sewer means a sewer which carries sewage and to which storm, surface and ground waters are not intentionally admitted. 
    Sewage means a combination of the water-carried wastes from residences, business buildings, institutions or industrial establishments, together with such ground, surface and stormwaters as may be present. 
    Sewage treatment plant means any arrangement of devices an structures used for treating sewage. 
    Sewage works means all facilities for collecting, pumping, treating and disposing of sewage. 
    Sewer means a pipe or conduit for carrying sewage. 
    Significant industrial user shall be defined as follows: 
(1)	Has a process wastewater* flow of 25,000 gallons or more per average work day;
(*Excludes sanitary, noncontact cooling and boiler blowdown wastewater) 
(2)	Contributes a process waste stream which makes up five percent or more of the average dry weather hydraulic or organic capacity of the POTW; 
(3)	Is subject to categorical pretreatment standards; or
(4)	Has significant impact, either singularly or in combination with other significant dischargers, on the treatment works or the quality of its effluent. 
    Slug load shall mean any discharge at a flow rate or concentration which could cause a violation of the prohibited discharge standard in subsection 82-138 (4) of this article or any discharge of a nonroutine, episodic nature, including but not limited to an accidental spill or a noncustomary batch discharge. 
    Standard methods shall mean the latest edition of "Standard Methods for the Examination of Water and Wastewater," published by the American Public Health Association, Water Pollution Control Federation and American Water Works Association. 
    State shall mean the Commonwealth of Virginia. 
    Storm sewer shall mean a sewer for conveying storm, surface, and other waters, which is not intended to be transported to a treatment works. 
    Surface water shall mean: 
(1)	All waters which are currently used, were used in the past, or may be susceptible to use in interstate or foreign commerce, including all waters which are subject to the ebb and flow of the tide; 
(2)	All interstate waters, including interstate "wetlands";
(3)	All other waters, such as inter/intrastate lakes, rivers, streams (including intermittent streams), mudflats, sandflats, "wetlands," sloughs, prairie potholes, wet meadows, playa lakes, or natural ponds, the use, degradation, or destruction of which would affect or could affect interstate or foreign commerce including any such waters: 
a.	Which are or could be used by interstate or foreign travelers for recreational or other purposes; 
b.	From which fish or shellfish are or could be taken and sold in interstate or foreign commerce; or 
c.	Which are used or could be used for industrial purposes by industries in interstate commerce. 
(4)	All impoundments of waters otherwise defined as surface waters under this definition;
(5)	Tributaries of waters identified in subsections (1) through (6) of this definition;
(6)	A wetlands adjacent to waters other than waters that are themselves wetlands, identified in subsections (1) through (6) of this definition. 
    Suspended solids shall mean the total suspended matter that either floats on the surface of, or is in suspension in, water or wastewater as determined by standard methods. 
    Treatment facility shall mean only those mechanical power-driven devices necessary for the transmission and treatment of pollutants (e.g., pump stations, unit treatment processes). 
    Treatment works shall mean any devices and systems used for the storage, treatment, recycling and/or reclamation of sewage or liquid industrial waste, or other waste necessary to recycle or reuse water, including intercepting sewers, outfall sewers, sewage collection systems, individual systems, pumping, power and other equipment and their appurtenances, extensions, improvements, remodeling, additions, or alterations, and any works, including land that will be an integral part of the treatment process or is used for ultimate disposal of residues resulting from such treatment, or any other method or system used for preventing, abating, reducing, storing, treating, separating, or disposing of municipal waste or industrial waste, including waste in combined sewer water and sanitary sewer systems. 
    Toxics shall mean any of the pollutants designated by federal regulations pursuant to Section 307 (a) (1) of the Act. 
    User shall mean a source of wastewater discharge into a POTW. 
    User permit shall mean a document issued by the POTW to the user that permits the connection and/or introduction of wastes into the treatment works under the provisions of this article. 
    VPDES shall mean Virginia Pollutant Discharge Elimination System permit program, as administered by the Commonwealth of Virginia. 
    Wastewater shall mean a combination of liquid and water-carried wastes from residences, commercial buildings, industries, and institutions, together with any groundwater, surface water, or storm water that may be present. 
    WPCF shall mean the water pollution control federation. 
(Ord. of 6-3-2008)
Sec. 82-82. - General definitions. 
    Unless the context of usage indicates otherwise, the meaning of terms in this article and not defined in section 82-81 above, shall be as defined in the Glossary: Water and Wastewater Control Engineering prepared by Joint Editorial Board of the American Public Health Association, American Society of Civil Engineers, American Water Works Association, and Water Pollution Control Federation, Copyright 1969. 
(Ord. of 6-3-2008)
Secs. 82-83-82-89. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - GENERAL PROVISIONS 

Sec. 82-90. - Purpose. 
    The purpose of this article is to provide for the maximum possible beneficial public use of the town treatment works through regulation of sewer construction, sewer use, and wastewater discharges; to provide for equitable distribution of the costs of the treatment works; and to provide procedures for complying with the requirements contained herein. 
(Ord. of 6-3-2008)
Sec. 82-91. - Scope. 
(a)	The definitions of terms used in this article are found in division 1. The provisions of this article shall apply to the discharge of all wastewater to treatment works of the town. This article provides for use of the town's treatment works, regulation of sewer construction, control of the quantity and quality of wastewater discharged, wastewater pretreatment, equitable distribution of costs, assurance that existing customers' capacity will not be preempted, approval of sewer construction plans, issuance of user permits, minimum sewer connection standards and conditions, and penalties and other procedures in cases of violation of this article. 
(b)	This article shall apply to the town and to persons outside the town who are, by contract, permit or agreement with the town, users of the town treatment works. 
(Ord. of 6-3-2008)
Sec. 82-92. - Administration. 
    Except as otherwise provided herein, the manager shall administer, implement, and enforce the provisions of this article. 
Fees and charges. 
(1)	All fees and charges payable under the provisions of this article shall be paid to the town. Such fees and charges shall be as set forth herein or as established in the latest monthly sewer rates, sewer access fees, and monthly sewer rates as provided by general council resolution. 
(2)	All user fees, penalties and charges collected under this article (and the treatment works user charge ordinance) shall be used for the sole purpose of constructing, operating or maintaining the treatment works of the town, or the retirement of debt incurred for same. 
(3)	All fees and charges payable under the provisions of this ordinance are due and payable upon the receipt of notice of charges. Unpaid charges shall become delinquent and shall be subject to penalty and interest charges as provided for in section 82-57. 
(Ord. of 6-3-2008)
Sec. 82-93. - Inspections. 
(a)	The manager or their designee, or authorized state or federal officials, bearing the proper credentials and identification, shall be permitted to enter all premises where an effluent source or treatment system is located at any reasonable time for the purposes of inspection, observation, measurement, sampling and/or copying records of the wastewater discharge to ensure that discharge to the treatment works is in accordance with the provisions of this article. 
(b)	The manager, bearing proper credentials and identification, shall be permitted to enter all private property through which the town holds an easement for the purposes of inspection, observation, measurement, sampling, repair, and maintenance of any of the town's treatment works lying within the easement. All entry, and any subsequent work on the easement, shall be done in final accordance with the terms of the easement pertaining to the private property involved. 
(c)	While performing any necessary work on private properties referred to in subsections (a) and (b) above, the (manager) shall observe all safety and occupational rules established by the owner or occupant of the property and applicable to the premises. 
(Ord. of 6-3-2008)
Sec. 82-94. - Vandalism. 
    No person shall maliciously, willfully, or negligently break, damage, destroy, uncover, deface, or tamper with any structure, appurtenance or equipment which is a part of the town's treatment works. Any person who violates this section shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction, is punishable by a fine in an amount not to exceed $250.00. 
(Ord. of 6-3-2008)
Sec. 82-95. - Separability. 
    If any provision of these regulations, or the application of any provision of these regulations to any person or circumstances, is held invalid, the application of such provision to other persons or circumstances, and the remainder of the regulations, shall not be affected thereby. 
(Ord. of 6-3-2008)
Sec. 82-96. - Amendments of the article. 
    Public notice shall be given in accordance with applicable provisions of the Town Charter, other town ordinances, state and federal law, prior to adoption of any amendments of this article. 
(Ord. of 6-3-2008)
Secs. 82-97-82-105. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - USE OF TOWN'S TREATMENT WORKS AND TREATMENT FACILITY 

Sec. 82-106. - Waste disposal. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to place, deposit, or permit to be deposited in any condition that may be considered as an unsanitary or unhygienic manner on public or private property within the town, or in any area under the jurisdiction of said town, any human or animal excrement, garbage, or other objectionable waste except where suitable treatment. 
(Ord. of 6-3-2008)
Cross reference- Animals, ch. 10. 
Sec. 82-107. - Wastewater discharges. 
    It shall be unlawful under state and federal law to discharge without a VPDES permit to any natural outlet within the town or in any area under its jurisdiction. Wastewater discharges to the town's treatment works are not authorized unless permitted by the manager in accordance with provisions of this article. 
(Ord. of 6-3-2008)
Sec. 82-108. - Wastewater disposal. 
    Except as provided in this article, it shall be unlawful to construct or maintain any privy, privy vault, septic tank, cesspool, or other facility intended or used for the disposal of wastewater. 
(Ord. of 6-3-2008)
Sec. 82-109. - Connection to treatment works required. 
    The owner of any house, building, or property which is used for commercial, industrial and/or residential purposes, abutting on any street, alley, or rights-of-way in which there is or may be located a sewer connected to the treatment works of the town, is required at the owner's expense to install suitable toilet facilities therein, and to connect such facilities directly to the proper sewer in accordance with the provisions of this article, within 90 days after notice that sewer is available within 100 feet of the property line. This section shall not apply to any person served by a privately constructed, owned, operated, and maintained sewer and treatment facility which discharges directly to a natural outlet in accordance with the provisions of this article and applicable state and federal laws. 
(Ord. of 6-3-2008)
Secs. 82-110-82-115. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 4. - BUILDING SEWERS AND CONNECTIONS[4] 

Footnotes: 
--- (4) --- 
Cross reference- Buildings and building regulations, ch. 14.

Sec. 82-116. - Connection permit. 
(a)	No person shall uncover, make any connections with, use, alter, or disturb any wastewater sewer or storm sewer without first obtaining a written permit from the manager. 
(b)	There shall be three classes of permits for connections to the town's treatment works and treatment facilities. 
Class I-Residential 
Class II-Industrial 
Class III-Commercial 
In all cases, the owner shall make application for a permit to connect to the town's treatment works on a form furnished by the town. The permit application shall be supplemented by wastewater information required to administer this article. A permit and inspection fee shall be paid to the town at the time the application is filed. Fees are based upon the latest sewer access fee schedule as provided by general council resolution. 
(c)	Connections to a storm sewer shall be subject to a permit. Such connections shall be subject to the provisions of this article and the approval of the manager. 
(Ord. of 6-3-2008)
Sec. 82-117. - Connection costs. 
    The costs and expenses incidental to the building sewer installation and connection to the town's treatment works shall be borne by the owner. The owner shall indemnify the town from any loss or damage that may directly or indirectly be occasioned by the installation of the building sewer. 
(Ord. of 6-3-2008)
Sec. 82-118. - Separate connections required. 
    A separate and independent building sewer shall be provided for every building except where one building stands at the rear of another on an interior lot and no private sewer is available or can be constructed to the rear building through an adjoining alley, courtyard, or driveway. When this occurs, the building sewer serving the front building may be extended to the rear building and the whole considered as one building sewer. The town assumes no obligation or responsibility for damage caused by or resulting from any single building sewer which serves two buildings. 
(Ord. of 6-3-2008)
Sec. 82-119. - Existing building sewers. 
    Existing building sewers may be used for connection of new buildings only when they are found, on examination and testing by the manager, to meet the requirements of this article. 
(Ord. of 6-3-2008)
Sec. 82-120. - Building sewer design. 
    The size, slope, alignment, construction materials, trench excavation and backfill methods, pipe placement, jointing and testing methods used in the construction and installation of a building sewer shall conform to the building and plumbing code or other applicable requirements of the town and Shenandoah County. For town utilities reference the town's standards and specifications manual. 
(Ord. of 6-3-2008; Ord. of 10-8-2014)
Sec. 82-121. - Building sewer elevation. 
    Whenever practicable, the building sewer shall be brought to a building at an elevation below the basement floor. In buildings in which any building drain is too low to permit gravity flow to the town's treatment works, wastewater carried by such building drain shall be lifted by an approved means and discharged to a building sewer draining to the town sewer. 
(Ord. of 6-3-2008)
Sec. 82-122. - Surface runoff and groundwater drains. 
(a)	No person shall connect roof, foundation, areaway, parking lot, roadway, or other surface runoff or groundwater drains to any sewer which is connected to a treatment works unless such connection is authorized in writing by the manager. The connection of such drains shall conform to codes specified in subsection 82-123(a) or as specified by the manager as a condition of approval of such connection. 
(b)	Except as provided in subsection (a) above, roof, foundation, areaway, parking lot, roadway, or other surface runoff or groundwater drains shall discharge to natural outlets or storm sewers. 
(Ord. of 6-3-2008)
Sec. 82-123. - Conformance to applicable codes. 
(a)	The connection of a building sewer into a treatment works shall conform to the requirements of the building and plumbing code or other applicable requirements of the town, or the procedures set forth in appropriate specifications of the Commonwealth of Virginia Sewerage Regulations, Uniform Building Code of Virginia, and American Society of Testing Materials. The connections shall be made gas-tight and water-tight and verified by proper testing. Any deviation from the prescribed procedures and materials must be approved in writing by the manager before installation. 
(Ord. of 6-3-2008)
Sec. 82-124. - Connection inspection. 
    The applicant for a building sewer or other drainage connection permit shall notify the manager when such sewer or drainage connection is ready for inspection prior to its connection to the town's treatment works. Such connection inspections and testing as deemed necessary by the manager shall be made by the manager or his designee. 
(Ord. of 6-3-2008)
Sec. 82-125. - Excavation guards and property restoration. 
    Excavations for building sewer installation shall be adequately guarded with barricades and lights so as to protect the public from hazard. Streets, sidewalks, parkways, and other public property disturbed in the course of the work shall be restored in a manner satisfactory to the town. 
(Ord. of 6-3-2008)
Sec. 82-126. - Protection of capacity for existing users. 
    The manager shall not issue a permit for any class of connection to the town's treatment works or treatment facilities unless there is sufficient capacity, not legally committed to other users, in the treatment works and treatment facilities to convey and adequately treat the quantity of wastewater which the requested connection will add to the treatment works or treatment facility. The manager may permit such a connection if there are legally binding commitments to provide the needed capacity. 
(Ord. of 6-3-2008)
Secs. 82-127-82-135. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 5. - CONDITIONS TO USE THE TOWN'S TREATMENT WORKS 

Sec. 82-136. - Special uses of treatment works. 
    All discharges of storm water, surface water, groundwater, roof runoff, subsurface drainage, or other waters not intended to be treated in the treatment facility shall be made to storm sewers or natural outlets designed for such discharges, except as authorized under subsection 82-122(a). Any connection, drain, or arrangement which will permit any such waters to enter any other sewer shall be deemed to be a violation of this section and this article. 
(Ord. of 6-3-2008)
Sec. 82-137. - Industrial user, general prohibition upon 
    An industrial user shall not introduce any pollutants into the town's treatment works which will pass through or interfere with the operation or performance of the treatment facilities. 
(Ord. of 6-3-2008)
Sec. 82-138. - Restricted discharges. 
(a)	No person shall discharge or cause to be discharged to any of the town's treatment works any substances, materials, waters, or wastes in such quantities or concentrations which do or are likely to: 
(1)	Create a fire or explosion hazard including, but not limited to, gasoline, benzene, naphtha, fuel oil, or other flammable or explosive liquid, solid, or gas; waste stream with a closed cup flashpoint of less than 140 degrees Fahrenheit or 60 degrees Centigrade using test methods specified in 40 CFR 261.21; 
(2)	Cause corrosive damage or hazard to structures, equipment, or personnel of the wastewater facilities, but in no case discharges with the following properties: 
a.	Having a pH lower than 5.0 or greater than 11.0
(3)	Cause obstruction to the flow in sewers, or other interference with the operation of treatment facilities due to accumulation of solid or viscous materials; 
(4)	Constitute a rate of discharge or substantial deviation from normal rates of discharge, ("slug discharge"), sufficient to cause interference in the operation and performance of the treatment facilities; 
(5)	Contain heat in amounts which are likely to accelerate the biodegradation of wastes, causing the formation of excessive amounts of hydrogen sulfide in the treatment works or inhibit biological activity in the treatment facilities, but in no case shall the discharge of heat cause the temperature in the town wastewater sewer to exceed 65 degrees C (150 degrees F) or the temperature of the influent to the treatment facilities to exceed 40 degrees C (104 degrees F) unless the facilities can accommodate such heat and the town has obtained prior approval from the approval authority; 
(6)	Contain more than 100 milligrams per liter of nonbiodegradable oils of mineral or petroleum origin; 
(7)	Contain floatable oils, fat, or grease;
(8)	Contain noxious gases, vapors or fumes, malodorous gas or substance in quantities that may cause a public nuisance or cause acute human or safety problems;
